PRESIDENT
PROPOSED COMMUNITY DEVELOPMENT BLOCK GRANT PROGRAM

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 31 , 2005 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
transmitted herewith are the recommended projects for the 2005 Community Development Block Grant
Program (CDBG), the Emergency Shelter Grants (ESG) Program, and the proposed use of the HOME
Investment Partnerships Program (HOME). The Cook County Community Development Advisory
Council adopted these recommendations at a public hearing held on May 12, 2005.
The amount of CDBG funds requested was $31, 184,004.00. The amount of CDBG funds available for
programming is $14,112,872.00. The proposed use of CDBG funds will provide a 100% benefit to low
and moderate income persons.
The amount of ESG funds requested was $1, 115,450.00. The amount of ESG funds available for
programming is $464,246.00. The propose use of ESG funds provides essential services and
maintenance/operational costs for homeless shelters in suburban Cook County, as well as programs for
homeless prevention.
The amount of HOME Investment Partnerships Program funds granted by the U.S. Department of
Housing and Urban Development (HUD) is $6,297,078.00. Additionally, the County will receive
$354,822.00 in fiscal year 2003 funds and $398,640.00 for fiscal 2004 and $227 ,313.00 in fiscal year
2005 for a combined total of $980,775.00, for the new American Dream Down Payment Initiative
recently announced by HUD. Applications for eligible HOME projects are accepted throughout the year.
The proposed use of all funds must be incorporated into the County's Annual Action Plan for submittal to
HUD.

1890

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 2 1, 2005

Prior to submitting required documents to HUD, Cook County is required by Executive Order 12372,
Intergovernmental Review of Federal Programs, to submit proposed projects to the Northeastern Illinois
Planning Commission and the Illinois State Clearinghouse for their review and release to HUD. The
County must also publish the description of the Annual Action Plan. All documents and certifications
must be submitted to HUD no later than August 15, 2005.
I respectfully request approval of the recommended CDBG and ESG projects, the proposed use of the
HOME funds, and that, I or the Chief Administrative Officer of the County of Cook, or his designee, be
authorized to execute, on behalf of the County of Cook, any and all documents necessary to further the
programs approved herein, including, but not limited to, subrecipient agreements, intergovernmental
agreements, amendments and modifications thereto, loan documents, lien assignments, releases of
mortgages and liens, and mortgage assumptions.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the communication be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 271729). The motion
carried unanimously.

PROPOSED ORDINANCES
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN and EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioners
Co-Sponsored by
ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI and BOBBIE L. STEELE,
County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
DISPLACED BUILDING SERVICE WORKERS PROTECTION ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article 7, Section 6a of
the Illinois Constitution of 1970 with power to regulate those matters which pertain to its government and
affairs.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT ENACTED, by the People of the County of Cook, Illinois, represented by
the Cook County Board of Commissioners:
Section 1: Title. This Ordinance may be cited as the Displaced Building Service Workers Protection
Ordinance.Â·
Section 2: Definitions. In this Ordinance:
"Building service" means work performed in connection with the care or maintenance of an existing
building and includes, but is not limited to, work performed by a watchman, security officer, door staff,
building cleaner, maintenance technician, handyman, janitor, elevator operator, window cleaner, building
engineer and groundskeeper.
"Building service contract" means a contract let to any covered employer for the furnishing of building
services and includes any subcontract for such services.
"Building service contractor" means any person who enters into a building service contract.
"Building service employee" means any person employed as a building service employee by a covered
employer who has been regularly assigned to a building on a full or part-time basis for at least 90 days
immediately preceding any transition in employment subject to this Section except for (i) persons who are
managerial, supervisory, or confidential employees, provided that this exemption shall not apply to
building engineers for existing properties, (ii) persons earning in excess of $25 per hour from a covered
employer, and (iii) persons regularly scheduled to work fewer than 6 hours per week at a building.
"County of Cook" means any city, township, administration, department, division, bureau, board or
commission, or a corporation, institution, or agency of government, the expenses of which are paid in
whole or in part from the County treasury.

1892

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

"Covered employer" means any person who owns or manages real property, either on its own behalf or
for another person, or any person who contracts or subcontracts with an owner or manager of real
property within the County of Cook for real estate, including, but not limited to, housing cooperatives,
condominium associations, building managing agents, and any building service contractor provided,
however, that the requirements of this Ordinance shall not apply to (i) residential buildings under 50
units, (ii) commercial office, institutional, or retail buildings of less than 75,000 square feet, (iii) any
building in which the County of Cook or any governmental entity, the head or majority of members of
which are appointed by one or more officers of the County of Cook, occupies 50% or more of the rentable
square footage, or (iv) any building that is owned or operated by a hospital or hospital affiliate as defined
in the Hospital Licensing Ordinance.
"Person" means any individual, proprietorship, partnership, joint venture, corporation, limited liability
company, trust, association, or other entity that may employ persons or enter into service contracts, but
shall not include the City of Chicago, the County of Cook, and the federal government or any other entity,
or any individual or entity managing real property for a governmental entity.
"Successor employer" means a covered employer that (i) has been awarded a building service contract
to provide, in whole or in part, building services that are substantially similar to those provided under a
service contract that has recently been terminated, or (ii) has purchased or acquired control of property in
which building service employees were employed.
Section 3: Protection for building service employees.
(a) No less than 15 calendar days before tenninating any building service contract, any covered
employer shall request the terminated contractor to provide the successor employer and any collective
bargaining representative of any of the affected employees a full and accurate list containing the name,
address, date of hire, and employment occupation classification of each building service employee
employed on the notice date at the site or sites covered by the terminated contract.
(b) No less than 15 calendar days before transferring a controlling interest in any covered
building in which building service employees are employed, any covered employer shall provide to the
successor employer and any collective bargaining representative of any of the affected employees a full
and accurate list containing the name, address, date of hire, and employment occupation classification of
each building service employee currently employed at the site or sites covered by the transfer of
controlling interest.
(c) Any covered employer shall provide to the successor employer and any collective bargaining
representati ve of any of the affected employees a full and accurate list containing the name, address, date
of hire, and employment occupation classification of each building service employee currently employed
at the site or sites covered by the tenninated building service contract no more than 7 calendar days after
notice that its building service contract has been tenninated.
(d) When providing the notice required under this Section, each covered employer shall ensure
that a notice to building service employees is posted setting forth the rights provided under this Section
and which includes a copy of the list provided under the proceeding Sections, and that such notice is also
provided to the employees' collective bargaining representative, if any. The notice and list shall be posted
in the same location and manner that other statutorily required notices to employees are posted at the
affected site or sites.

1893

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDING S FOR JUNE 2 1, 2005

(e) A successor employer shall retain for a 90-day transition employment period at the affected
site or sites those building service employees of the terminated building service contractor and its
subcontractors, or other covered employer, employed at the site or sites covered by the terminated
building service contract or owned or operated by the former covered employer.
(f) If at any time the successor employer detennines that fewer building service employees are
required to perform building services at the affected building than had been perfonning such services
under the former employer, the successor employer shall retain the predecessor building service
employees by seniority within job classification; provided that during such a 90-day transition period, the
successor employer shall maintain a preferential hiring list of those building service employees not
retained at the building who shall be given a right of first refusal to any jobs within their classification
that becomes available during that period.
(g) Except as provided in subsection (f), during such 90-day period, the successor contractor shall
not discharge without cause an employee retained pursuant to this Section.
(h) At the end of the 90-day transition period, the successor employer shall perfonn a written
perfonnance evaluation for each employee retained pursuant to this Section. If the employee's
perfonnance during such 90-day period is satisfactory, the successor contractor shall offer the employee
continued employment under the tenns and conditions established by the successor employer or as
required by law.

Section 4: Violation.
(a) A building service employee who has been discharged or not retained in violation of this
Ordinance may bring an action in court against a successor contractor and covered employer for violation
of any obligation imposed pursuant to this Ordinance.
(b) The court shall have the authority to order injunctive relief to prevent or remedy a violation of
any obligation imposed pursuant to this Ordinance.
(c) If the court finds that by reason of a violation of any obligation imposed pursuant to
subsection (b), a building service employee has been discharged in violation of this Section, it shall
award:

(I) Back pay for each day during which the violation continues, which shall be calculated
at a rate of compensation not less than the higher of (i) the average regular rate of pay
received by the employee during the last 3 years of the employee's employment in the
same occupation classification; or (ii) the final regular rate received by the employee.
(2) Costs of benefits the successor employer would have incurred for the employee under
the successor contractor's or employer's benefit plans.
(3) The building service employee's reasonable attorney's fees and costs.
(d) In any such action, the court shall have the authority to order the terminated contractor or
fonner employer to provide the successor employer with the information required pursuant to Section
10(c) of this Ordinance.

Section 5: Exemptions.
The provisions of this Ordinance do not apply:

1894

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

(I) To any successor employer that, on or before, the effective date of the transfer of control from
a predecessor covered employer to the successor employer to the commencement of services by a
successor building service contractor, agrees to assume, or to be bound by, the collective bargaining
agreement of the predecessor covered building service employees, provided that the collective bargaining
agreement provides tenns and conditions for the discharge or laying off of employees.
(2) Where there is no existing collective bargaining agreement as described in subdivision (I), to
any successor employer that agrees, on or before the effective date of the transfer of control from a
predecessor covered employer to the successor employer or the commencement of services by a successor
building service contractor, to enter into a new collective bargaining agreement covering its building
service employees, provided that the collective bargaining agreement provides terms and conditions for
the discharged or laying off of employees.
(3) To any successor employer whose building service employees will be accredited to a
bargaining unit with a pre-exis ting collective bargaining agreement, provided that the collective
bargaining agreement provides terms and conditions for the discharged or layin'g off of employees.
(4) To any covered employer that obtains a written commitment from a successor employer that
the successor employer's building service employees will be covered by a collective bargaining agreement
falling within subdivision (1), (2), or (3).

Section 6: Effective date.
This Ordinance takes effect upon becoming law.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 271732). The motion
carried unanimously.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE

ARTICLE I.
GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section l.1

Short Title

This Ordinance shall be cited and known as the "Cook County Jail Diversion Program"

1895

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Section 1.2

Preamble

WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of government as defined in Article VII, Section
6(a) of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, and as such may exercise any power, and perform
any function pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has an ongoing responsibility for protecting the health and safety of its
residents and remains committed to public service that is efficient, equitable and accountable; and
WHEREAS, approximately 20% or more than 6,000 of Cook County inmates, per 2004 U.S. Justice
Department statistics, have diagnoses of mental illness and enter the penal system by committing crimes
that may be, totally or in part, attributable to their mental illness; and
WHEREAS, the rate of recidivism, approximated to be near 80% among the mentally ill population, is
commonly referred to as the " revolving door syndrome" which makes it more difficult to comply with the
Federal Consent Decree on overcrowding in Cook County Jail; and
WHEREAS, each non-violent offender who is diverted from incarceration, Cook County saves an
estimated $ 1,800/per month/per person by avoiding the cost of prosecution and court expenses not
including the cost of healthcare; and
WHEREAS, it has been documented that the number of arrests, the length of jail-time, as well as hospital
stays among the mentally ill are substantially reduced when diversionary measures are employed that
provide appropriate assessment and treatment as an alternatives to incarceration; and
WHEREAS, the establishment of a Cook County Jail Diversion Program in partnership with the State of
Illinois, local law enforcement, and community-based mental health and social service providers will
reduce Cook County' s jail population and improve the quality of mental healthcare in Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, BY THE PRESIDENT AND THE COOK COUNTY
BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS TO ESTABLISH A COOK COUNTY JAIL DIVERSION
PROGRAM FOR MENTALLY ILL AND/OR ALCOHOL AND SUBSTANCE DEPENDENT
ARRESTEES.
ARTICLE II.
DEFINITIONS
Section 2.1

Definitions

For purposes of this Ordinance, whenever any of the following words, terms or definitions is used, they
shall have the meaning ascribed to them in this section:
Case Management: A process to supervise and assist the mentally ill detainee in achieving his or her
individualized treatment plan.
Chemical Dependent: Anyone who is addicted to drugs and/or other chemical substances.
Community Based Mental Health Service Providers: Individuals in local organizations and health
facilities with expertise in providing comprehensive psychological, emotional and/or psychiatric services,
in accordance with standard practices under the Illinois State Mental Health Code, in addition to standard
practices adopted by the Illinois Psychological Association.

1896

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Detainees: Mentally ill and/or alcohol and substance dependent who are held m custody by law
enforcement.
Misdemeanors: Any offense for which a sentence to a term of imprisonment, other than a penitentiary
for less than one year may be imposed (720 ILCS 5/2-11 ) (from Ch. 38, par. 2-11 ), Sec 2-11 :
730 ILCS 5/5-9-1 and 5/5-8-3
Class A: Up to $25,000 Fine and/or up to 1 year in Jail
Class B: Up to $1,500 Fine and/or up to 6 months in Jail
Class C: Up to $1,500 Fine and/or up to 30 days in Jail
Felony: An offense for which a sentence to death or a term of imprisonment in a penitentiary for one
year or more. (720 ILCS 5/2-7) (from Ch. 38, par. 2-7), Sec 2-7:
730 ILCS 5/5-8-1 and 5/5-9-1
Class 2 Felony: Up to $25,000 Fine and/or 3 to 7 years in Penitentiary
Class 3 Felony: Up to $25,000 Fine and/or 2 to 5 years in Penitentiary
Class 4 Felony: Up to $25,000 Fine and/or I to 3 years in Penitentiary
*FELONY, INCREASES PENALTY TO 15-20-25-LIFE
Jail Diversion: An alternative to incarceration.
Mentally Ill: Persons who have been clinically diagnosed as being psychologically or emotionally
impaired.
Pre-Booking Diversion: Intervention prior to any formal charges being filed against a detainee.
Post Booking Diversion: Intervention at the State' s Attorney' s Office which provides an alternative to
prosecution.
Psychological Assessment: An examination by a licensed clinician as defined in accordance with
provisions set forth in Article III , Section 3.4, Subsection B of this Ordinance.
Restitution: An act of restoring or a condition of being restored, restoration of something to its rightful
owner and making good of or giving an equivalent for some injury.

ARTICLE III.
CREATION OF COOK COUNTY JAIL DIVERSION PILOT PROGRAM
Section 3.1
A.

Scope of Services

The scope of services shall include an individualized psychological evaluation and assessment,
referrals for appropriate service including housing, and case management. The program must be
designed to reduce the number of mentally ill and alcohol and substance dependent detainees
entering into the Cook County Jail, and afford greater opportunities for crisis intervention and
essential supportive services.

1897

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

B.

To the extent possible, mental health and substance abuse service providers who participate in the
jail diversion program shall be those who are already receiving funds from Federal, State,
County, and/or Local units of governments for Mental Health and/or Substance Abuse services.
All Cook County contracts if any shall be perfonnance based and renewed contingent upon the
quality and quantity of service rendered the previous year. Each participating agency must have
an individualized service plan for each participant in their program. The plan shall be developed
by a licensed professional in the State of Illinois in the field of mental health and/or the treatment
of alcohol and substance dependent persons. This plan must be in collaboration with the
appropriate law enforcement officials and the criminal justice system when applicable. The
treatment plan shall be consistent with standard practices under the lllinois State Mental Health
Code, in addition to standard practices adopted by the Illinois Psychological Association.

C.

A regional 24-hour mentally ill crisis center shall be established to be utilized by local law
enforcement when there is no available service in the impact area. The crisis center shall be
funded and governed by the intergovernmental agreement established in accordance with
provisions set forth in Article III, Section 3.5, Subsection C of this Ordinance.

D.

In those cases where a detainee has been diagnosed by the appropriate clinician as being mentally

ill and/or alcohol and substance dependent and who is not on Medicaid/Medicare, the Cook
County Bureau of Health Services shall make every concerted effort to process their application
with the appropriate governmental body and any other third party reimbursement that the detainee
is entitled.

Section 3.2

Target Population

Cook County's Jail Diversion Pilot Program shall focus on diverting the following categories:

A.

The mentally ill and/or alcohol and substance dependent arrestees detained for Class B and C
misdemeanors.

B.

Mentally ill and/or alcohol and substance dependent detainees held for trial on Class A
misdemeanor and Class 4 felony charges.

Section 3.3

Target Communities

The targeted areas currently used by the Cook County Mental Health Court and the Village of Maywood.

Section 3.4

Jail Diversion

This jail diversion pilot program is designed to strengthen existing jail diversion efforts which are
currently used by some local law enforcement officials such as station adjustments, peer jury's, special
courts, and other alternatives to incarceration.
A.

This program will be composed of four levels each of which will have agreed-upon conditions by
all invol ved parties, tailored to particular circumstances, for which arrestees shall be held
accountable. The four levels are as follows:

1898

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

(1) Pre-booking Diversion:
This level shall be sought for mentally ill and alcohol and substance dependent detainees for
Class B and C misdemeanors as often as possible. The arresting officer shall be the first line of
contact and shall take, but not be limited to the following basic steps prior to any official charges
for minor and/or nuisance crimes:
a.
b.
c.
d.
e.
f.

g.
h.
1.

Attempt to resolve any crisis without hann to the suspect, general public, or Jaw enforcement
officials.
Refer directly to a hospital or treatment center when necessary.
Contact parent or guardian if mentally ill detainee is under seventeen.
Evaluate the situation and detennine ifthe suspect is potentially divertible.
Determine if detainee can be sent to his or her residence under conditions agreed upon by law
enforcement, detainee, parent(s) or guardian, and the victim of the crime.
Contact the participating mental health community service providers when necessary for
proper assessments and referrals for service intervention in accordance with provisions set
forth in Article III, Section 3.4, Sub-Section B of this Ordinance.
If local service is not available contact the 24-hour regional crisis center for service
intervention.
In cases where there is an injured party or damage to someone's property, all efforts for
restitution shall be explored and agreed upon by all parties involved.
Complete a detailed incident report.

(2) Post-Booking Diversion:
This level shall be sought at the State' s Attorney level for persons with a history of mental illness
and/or alcohol and substance abuse dependency who are detained for crimes that constitute Class
A misdemeanors and Class 4 felonies. The pre-arraignment investigation must include
immediate assessment by the appropriate clinicians as defined in accordance with provisions set
forth in Article III, Section 3.4, Subsection B of this Ordinance to determine if the suspect was
mentally ill or under the influence of alcohol or drugs at the time the crime was committed. A
preliminary hearing shall be conducted prior to arraignment to detennine whether or not the
suspect can be diverted rather than incarcerated. If a diversionary plan is agreed upon by all
parties involved, an individualized treatment and service plan shall be developed by the
appropriate clinician as defined in accordance wi th provisions set forth in Article III, Section 3.4,
Subsection B of this Ordinance. In cases where there is an injured party or damage to someone' s
property, all efforts for restitution shall be explored and agreed upon by all parties involved. The
case shall be referred to the appropriate participating community service provider when possible.
A case manager shall be assigned and report periodically to the State's Attorney's Office as to the
defendant's progress.
(3) Pre-Trial Arraignment Level:

This level shall continue to emphasize proper assessment and speedy trials for those detainees
who have been diagnosed by the appropriate clinicians as being mentally ill and/or alcohol and
substance dependent. If a defendant has been diagnosed as being mentally ill and/or alcohol and
substance dependent and is held over for trial, the Judge should immediately request the
appropriate service intervention. The case should be referred to the appropriate special court for
the mentally ill or drug addicted for trial with a specific timeframe for the trial to proceed.

1899

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 2 I, 2005

(4) Trial Level:
The Cook County Mental Health and Drug Courts shall continue to divert mentally ill and/or
alcohol and substance dependent defendants from the Cook County Jail. In cases where the
defendant has been found guilty of a Class A misdemeanor or a Class 4 felony and above and it
has been detennined by the courts that the defendant was mentally ill and/or alcohol and
substance dependent at the time the crime was committed, the diversion plan shall be developed
in collaboration with the appropriate clinician in accordance with provisions set forth in Article
III, Section 3.4, Subsection B of this Ordinance. A case manager should be assigned to the case
and report periodically back to the State's Attorney the status of the defendant ' s conduct in
accordance with his/her individualized service plans. In cases where the defendant is
institutionalized the arresting law enforcement agency shall be notified prior to the defendant
returning back to the community.
Nothing in Article III, Section 3.4, Subsection A 1-4 should be construed as infringement upon or
inhibit any existing diversion or alternative to incarceration programs in Cook County.

Section 3.5

Intergovernmental Agreement

An intergovernmental agreement shall be established between the Cook County Board of Commissioners,
the State of Illinois, and the participating local units of government. The agreement shall include but not
be limited to the following provisions:
A.

A memorandum of understanding as to the State of Illinois, County of Cook, and local
governments responsibility for the mentally ill population in Cook County.

B.

Shared resources.

C.

The establishment and funding of a 24-hour Mentally Ill Health Crisis Intervention Center.

D.

Standardized policies and procedures to ensure equal opportunity for the mentally ill and
alcohol and substance abuse dependent population to participate in the diversion program not
withstanding their place of residence.

ARTICLE IV.
ADVISORY PANEL
Section 4.1

Purpose

The purpose of the Advisory Panel is to establish a strong advocacy and resource group to enhance Cook
County' s effort to improve the quality of mental health services to the mentally ill and/or alcohol and
substance dependent population in Cook County, and to reduce this population in our Cook County Jail.
The eleven member panel shall be composed of persons with expertise in law enforcement, criminal
justice, assessment and treatment of the mentally ill and/or alcohol and substance dependent population.

Section 4.2

Structure

An eleven-member Advisory Panel will be established to develop operating rules and procedures and
criteria for implementation and evaluating the Cook County Jail Diversion Program.

1900

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

The Advisory Panel shall consist of eleven ( 11) members: one (I ) appointed by the Chief Judge, one ( l )
appointed by the Cook County Sheriff, two (2) appointed by the State's Attorney, one (I) appointed by
the Public Defender, two (2) appointed by the City of Chicago, one (1) appointed by the Village of
Maywood, three (3) appointed by the President of the Cook County Board: one (1) selected from the
Bureau of Mental Health Division, one ( I) selected from University of lllinois Jane Addams School of
Social Work, and one (1) selected from Ill inois Community Mental Health Providers Association.
This Advisory Panel's composition will reflect the demographics of the County as a whole. T hey shall
select officers from among their membership.

Section 4.3

Powers and Duties of Advisory Panel

The powers and duties of the Advisory Panel shall include but not be limited to the following:
A.

Establish administrative policies and procedures for implementation of the jail diversion program.

B.

To research current federal and state funding resources for service to the mentally ill and/or
alcohol and substance dependent population.

C.

Develop a feasibility study to determine the availability of essential mental health and/or alcohol
and substance dependent services at the community level to ensure a successful mental health
diversion program.

D.

Establish a structure by which we can maximize the use of existing resources and make them
readily available to law enforcement for appropriate referrals.

E.

Assist in establishing a collaborative relationship between the State of lllinois, County of Cook,
local municipalities and local community based mental health and substance abuse service
providers with emphasis on mutual goals, shared responsibilities and benefits.

F.

Review existing training curriculum for law enforcement officials and make recommendations for
change to enhance their ability where needed for identifying and processing mentally ill and/or
alcohol and substance dependent detainees.

G.

Establish criteria for measuring the outcome of the program.

H.

To devise a plan for minimizing cost through service integration and coordination.

I.

To lobby federal and state governments to improve funding resources for the program services.

J.

To apply for a grant fo r support staff to the Advisory Panel.

ARTICLE V.
ESTABLISHMENT OF A CENTRAL DATABASE
Section 5.1

Establishment of A Central Database

The Cook County State's Attorney' s Office shall maintain a central data base to help local Jaw
enforcement agencies identify and track any "repeat" offenders who may have been previously diagnosed
with a mental illness and alcohol and substance abuse.

1901

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

ARTICLE VI.

EVALUATIONS
Section 6.1

Police Evaluations

Evaluations of police responses shall be consistently conducted on a case-by-case basis to detennine the
quality of the process that law enforcement uses to intervene on behalf of the mentally ill and/or alcohol
and substance dependent detainees. Evaluation criteria shall include, but not be limited to the following:
A.

Was there any significant violence and hann done to the subject, the general public or law
enforcement officials during the process of apprehension?

B.

Was the crisis resolved on the scene? At the police station? Or elsewhere?

C.

Were family members alerted and included in the problem resolution process?

D.

Was the detainee transported or referred to the appropriate service provided when warranted?

E.

Was the detainee formally incarcerated? If so, for what length of time?

F.

Did Jaw enforcement take advantage of community-based resources and were the resources
readily available as well as suitable for the situation?

G.

Was this a "repeat encounter" with the detainee within a year, six months, 90 days, 45 days?

Section 6.2

Performance Measurement Standards

A.

Mental health perfonnance measurement shall be detennined by the Cook County Bureau of
Health Services in accordance with the Illinois State Mental Health Code, in addition to standard
practices adopted by the Illinois Psychological Association and the National Association of
Clinical Social Workers.

B.

Measurement outcome criteria shall include, but not be limited to the following:
1.
2.
3.
4.
5.
6.
7.
8.

Case management.
Total number of detainees seen per quarter.
Number of medical appointments made by detainee and percentage of those kept.
Documentation that confirms detainees living arrangements.
The amount of periodic follow-up conducted with family-based detainees to detennine if
basic needs were being met.
Current and accurate detainee records that are available for review by any appropriate
governmental agency.
Number of times, if any, detainee was re-arrested.
Progress report of the detainee's efforts in accordance with their individualized service
plan.
ARTICLE VII.
APPLICABILITY

Section 7.1

Applicability

As provided in Article VII, Section 6(c), of the State of Illinois Constitution of 1970, if this Ordinance
conflicts with an ordinance of a municipality, the municipal ordinance shall prevail within the pilot area.

1902

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

If a municipal ordinance regulates conduct which is prohibited under this Ordinance and provides
remedies, this Ordinance shall not apply within that municipal j urisdiction with respect to such conduct.
In all other circumstances, this Ordinance shall be enforceable within the municipal jurisdiction to the
extent permitted under the Illinois Constitution.

ARTICLE VIII.
SEVERABILITY
Section 8.1

Severability

If any article, paragraph, sentence, or clause of this Ordinance or the application thereof to any person is
for any reason deemed to be invalid or unconstitutional, such decision shall not affect any remaining
portion, section, or part thereof or application of this Ordinance to any person.

ARTICLE IX.
EFFECTIVE DA TE
Section 9.1

Effective Date

A.

Within one (1) year after the implementation of this Pilot Program, the Advisory Panel shall
report to the Cook County Board of Commissioners regarding the number of arrestees diverted,
the cost benefits to Cook County, the effectiveness and future viability of an expanded county
wide jail diversion program.

B.

This Ordinance shall take effect six (6) months after its passage and publication.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

referred to the Public Health Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 271734). The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Mandatory Garbage Service Ordinance

W HEREAS, Cook County currently has no ordinance requiring residents to have a refuse removal
service; and

1903

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

WHEREAS, municipalities throughout Cook County require their residents to use the services of a waste
disposal firm licensed with their respective municipality; and
WHEREAS, numerous incidents have arisen in which residents of unincorporated Cook County have
refused to dispose of their garbage in a safe and timely manner; and
WHEREAS, Cook County has had no recourse to address these situations as they arise.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that Cook County will institute the Mandatory Garbage
Service Ordinance requiring all residents in unincorporated Cook County to dispose of their garbage in
the following methods:
Section 1

(a) Lawful methods of disposal. All refuse produced on the premises of any residential dwelling
shall be disposed of by the person in possession of the premises by the acquisition of a refuse
removal service for each such residential dwelling from a waste disposal firm with pickup and
removal of such refuse by such waste disposal finn to be only from the premises on which the
refuse is generated and not from any location other than the premises on which the refuse is
generated. It shall be presumed that all residential dwellings in unincorporated Cook County
generate refuse. The Environmental Health Service Unit of the Cook County Department of
Public Health may waive the requirement of this section for a particular property only upon
receipt of a written request from the owner of the premises therefore, supported by clear and
convincing evidence, as detennined by the Environmental Health Service Unit of the Cook
County Department of Public Health, at their absolute discretion, that no refuse other than
recyclable materials are and will be generated by the occupants of the premises. The decision of
the Cook County Department of Public Health, Environmental Health Service Unit, to grant, or
deny, such a waiver request shall be final. Refuse produced on the premises of any residential
dwelling may be disposed of pursuant only to those specific additional methods of disposal
expressly authorized by, and approved pursuant to this Ordinance.
(b) Preparation of garbage. It shall be the duty of every person in possession of any premises to
cause all garbage produced on the premises to be thoroughly drained of all surplus liquid,
securely wrapped or bagged in paper or packed in a covered box or carton of such dimension as
will pennit its free passage into and out of the waste containers, and finally deposited after such
wrapping or bagging in such a waste container as soon as practicable after the same is produced
thereon. Materials of every character shall be securely wrapped or bound in such a manner as
may be necessary to prevent scattering and shall be deposited in a waste container or otherwise
deposited herein.
Section 2
(a) Penalties and Fines. The Environmental Health Service Unit of the Cook County Department of
Public Health shall have the authority to levy fines and issue citations to persons occupying
premises that fail to comply with Cook County ' s Mandatory Garbage Service Ordinance. The
Environmental Health Service Unit shall have the discretion of issuing a warning for a first
offense, $50 for a second offense and up to $250 for subsequent offenses.

1904

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be
referred to the Committee on Environmental Control. (Comm. No. 271735). The motion carried
unanimously.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN
and DEBORAH SIMS, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
A RESOLUTION TO ESTABLISH THE PARTNERS AGAINST ANIMAL CRUELTY
(PAAC) TASK FORCE AND TO PROMOTE EDUCATION WITHIN COOK COUNTY TO
REDUCE AND PREVENT ANIMAL ABUSE AND RELATED INTERPERSONAL
VIOLENCE
WHEREAS, criminal profiling experts associated with the Federal Bureau of Investigation have
identified a strong correlation between animal abuse and violence against humans and have documented
cruelty to animals as one of the traits which indicates the characteristics of a violent personality which is
demonstrated by the disproportionately high number of violent killers in the prison system, virtually every
serial killer, and recent cases of school violence; all of which have involved persons with a history of
animal abuse; and
WHEREAS, a strong correlation exists between animal abuse in a household and violence by the
offender against their spouse and their children and since intentional animal abuse is an early signal that
individuals, including young people, may perpetrate violent crimes against other individuals and since
many young children through their parents, friends or relatives have been exposed to Dog Fights,
witnessing and even participating, which desensitizes children to acts of violence, it is likely that children
exposed to Dog Fighting will commit acts of violence against humans and other crimes in the future as
studies have shown that the crimes attendant to Dog Fighting include organized gambling, narcotics
possession and/or distribution, and weapons violations; and
WHEREAS, Dog Fighting masked as "entertainment" is a fonn of violence against animals and a serious
problem throughout the United States, including Cook County, crossing all racial, ethnic and
socioeconomic lines. The State has enacted laws providing for the forfeiture of money, proceeds,
vehicles and real property acquired in whole or in part as a result of Dog Fighting, or the facilitation of
Dog Fighting, which require that the proceeds from the sale of properties forfeited and sold upon
conviction of Dog Fighting be utilized in the investigation and enforcement of laws including Dog
Fighting and animal cruelty; and

1905

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, the Partners Against Animal Cruelty (PAAC) Task Force was formed in September, 2004,
to coordinate a county-wide effort to abolish cruelty, neglect and violence involving animals in order to
improve the quality and safety of their lives as well as the lives and safety of the citizens of our
communities.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners recognizes
the establishment of Partners Against Animal Cruelty (PAAC), a volunteer organization governed by the
Cook County Board of Commissioners, comprised of an advisory board of fi ve to seven members, one
appointee from each of the seventeen ( 17) Commissioner Districts, and a representative from each of the
thirty (30) townships as well as law enforcement, animal control wardens, animal organizations, and
shelters; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners:

I.

Recognizes that individuals who abuse animals are more likely to commit more serious violent
crimes against humans.

2.

Urges social workers, teachers, mental health professionals, and others to be aware of the
connection between animal cruelty and human violence and to evaluate carefully and to monitor
closely individuals who have a history of abusing animals since this may indicate a propensity to
commit violence against other humans.

3.

Urges appropriate local and county agencies to encourage and support research to increase the
understanding of the connection between cruelty to animals and violence against humans in order
to utilize instances of animal abuse to identify and intervene with potentially violent individuals
and to assist in identifying and protecting children at risk of abuse and neglect.

4.

Urges agencies which are undertaking research on violent crime and its causes to incorporate
examination of the link between violence against animals and violence against humans.

5.

Urges local law enforcement officials, particularly prosecutors and judges, to treat cases of
animal cruelty seriously both because such cruelty is a reliable indicator of the potential for
domestic violence and other fonns of violence against humans.

6.

Commends the fine work of local animal control officials and humane investigators who help
enforce laws against animal abuse and urges these professionals to work more closely with local
law enfo rcement personnel to identify and prevent potential violence agai nst humans.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Murphy, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Public Health Subcommittee. (Comm. No. 271733). The motion carried unanimously.

This request is pursuant to the County Board's adoption of Item No. 176427 on September 16, 1991 that
all building and zoning pennit fees be waived for public entities defined as county, township,

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication, dated June I, 2005 from
MICHAEL E. LAMONT, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization to enter into a professional services
contract with McDonough Associates, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, for High-Rise Life Safety Evaluations
(LSE) at six (6) facilities within the City of Chicago. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body
approve this request.
Reason:

These Life Safety Evaluations (LSE) are required to be perfonned in accordance with the
newly revised Municipal Code of the City of Chicago, Section 13-1 96-206. The LSE must
be conducted on high-rise buildings that currently do not have sprinkler systems which
includes the County Building, First Municipal Courthouse, Criminal Courts Building, the
Hektoen Building, 1900 W. Polk Building and the Department of Corrections Division VII .
The LSE is a quantitative assessment of specific fire safety, means of egress and general
safety related elements of a building and a plan to bring the building into compliance through
repairs. The LSE is to be performed and submitted to the Chicago Department of Buildings
no later that January I, 2006.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $415,000.00. Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the communication be referred
to the Committee on Construction. (Comm . No. 2717 18). The motion carried unanimously.

appurtenances and shall be designated as Section: Ol-W3714-04-BR-MFT; and

and No/ 100 Dollars, ($2,000,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the

OFFICE OF THE CHIEF JUDGE
GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, date June 6, 2005 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization to accept a grant in the amount of $175,000.00 from the Annie E. Casey
Foundation. These funds will be used for the court's Juvenile Detention Alternative Initiatives (JDAI)
model site activities and for JDAI programming.
In 1998, the foundation recognized the Circuit Court of Cook County as a national model site for juvenile
detention refonn. This funding will be used to reimburse the court for expenses incurred in fulfilling its
model site duties, which include hosting delegations from jurisdictions around the country to study the
court's juvenile detention reform efforts. Funding will also provides contracted staff with support and
training for the court's JDAI programming.
This grant does not require a cash match.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $175,000.00. Funding period e~<teRsioR: January I, 2005
through December 31 , 2005 .

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Chief Judge
of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved, as amended and that the Proper Officials be authorized
to sign on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

JUDICIAL ADVISORY COUNCIL
INTERGOVERNMENTAL AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June l, 2005 from
DANIEL J. COUGHLIN, Executive Director, Judicial Advisory Council
On December 14, 2004, the Board granted authority to the Judicial Advisory Council to enter into thirtytwo intergovernmental participation agreements with municipalities within Cook County. These
participation agreements establish the framework pursuant to which the entities will be permitted to
participate in the Cook County Wireless Communication System. This project, a continuation of
President Stroger's efforts to provide a state of art wireless video and data interoperable communication
capabilities for first responders throughout Cook County, is funded through a grant from the United States
Department of Homeland Security Office of Domestic Preparedness and the Illinois Emergency
Management Agency. Phase I is approaching completion and the County is preparing to embark on
Phase II, which will involve the roll-out of equipment and network access to additional public entities
within Cook County.
At this time, the Judicial Advisory Council requests authorization to enter into additional
intergovernmental participation agreements with the remaining ninety-three municipalities of Cook
County which were not previously included in the communication presented to the Board on December
14, 2004, and amended on April 6, 2005. The authorization requested is intended to be flexible, allowing
the Judicial Advisory Council to enter into agreements with municipalities when the County is ready to
begin implementation within their jurisdictions, which will depend upon both funding and strategic
implementation considerations. Some of the agreements will not be entered into until additional funding
is received for Phase III.
I respectfully request that the Executive Director of the Cook County Judicial Advisory Council, or his
designee, on behalf of Cook County, be authorized to execute any and all documents necessary to further
the Interoperable Communication System project approved by the Cook County Board of Commissioners.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Executive
Director of the Judicial Advisory Council be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

COOPERATIVE EDUCATIONAL MASTER AGREEMENT
RENEWAL AND AMENDMENT

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 13, 2005 from
MICHELET. THOMPSON, Acting Chief Operating Officer, Provident Hospital of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew and amend the Sub-Agreement, Contract No.
02-43-1218 to the Master Affiliation Agreement for medical education and clinical programs in Family
Practice between Loyola University of Chicago, the Loyola University Medical Center and the Bureau of
Health Services.
The sub-agreement provides for continued assignment of resident physicians in the current Cook CountyLoyola Residency Program in Family Medicine and the continued University Faculty assignments at
Provident Hospital of Cook County. The amendments to the sub-agreement primarily reflect the
transition from Cook County resident FTE to Loyola FTE and that all residents participating in the
Family Practice Training Program are full time employees of Loyola University.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $5, 124,958.00. Contract period: July I, 2005 through June 30, 2006. (891-272
Account).

be authorized to renew and amend the Cooperative Educational Master Subagreement. The motion
carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF PUBLIC HEALTH
CONTRACT

Transmitting a Communication date June 7, 2005
STEPHEN A. MARTIN, JR., Ph.D., M.P.H., Chief Operating Officer, Department of Public Health
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Lifeline Shelter Systems,
Inc., Columbus, Ohio, for the purchase of one ( 1) first responder 53 foot bio safety level 3 sentinel
Hazardous Materials Laboratory/Command Center trailer and one (1) first responder 53 foot Medical
Assessment/Command Center trailer to be used by the Department of Public Health in the event of a bio
terrorism attack, health threat or natural disaster.
Reason:

The Department of Public Health's Bio-Terrorism Grant along with the Urban Area Security
Initiative Grant prepared a Request for Proposal (RFP) for these specialized custom made first
responder trailers. Five (5) firms who specialize in these custom trailers registered to be
included in the RFP process. Lifeline Shelter Systems, Inc. met all requirements and met the
projected budgetary parameters.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $746,192.00 [$342,119.00 - (903-549 Account);
and $404,073.00 - (769-549 Account)]. One time purchase. Requisition Nos. 59034951 and 57695554.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE PURCHASING AGENT
TERMINATION OF CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 14, 2005 from
RAYMOND C. ROBIN, Purchasing Agent
Re:

Contract Nos.
05- l 5-048H, Items 12, 14 and 26; and
04-15-131H, Item 6

Faustech Industries, Inc. has contracted to the County with respect to the above referenced contracts.
Faustech Industries, Inc. has notified Cook County in writing that they are no longer in business. On June
2, 2005 I issued a notice of default with regard to the above referenced contracts and informed Faustech
Industries, Inc. of the County's intention to terminate these contracts. Faustech Industries, Inc. notice of
default letter was returned to this office with a forwarding address. The default letter was then mailed to
the forwarding address.

1955

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

I hereby request that the above contracts be terminated by the County. Further, in order to ensure the
Bureau of Health Services receives essential medical supplies, without interruption, the following
arrangements are recommended to fulfill the requirements which were procured through these contracts.
With regard to these contracts, relatively small, procurements under ($25,000.00) remain to be made.
With respect to these contracts, I recommend that the contracted items be purchased through open market
quotation process as set forth in Section 10-1 8 of the Purchasing Ordinance until such time as new bids
can be solicited.
Note: See related item under the Bureau of Health Services.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Purchasing
Agent be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF RISK MANAGEMENT
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 2, 2005 from
JOHN L. HIBBETT, Director, Department of Risk Management
Re:

Pre-Paid Legal Service Benefits

requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with The Advocates Group,
Chicago, Illinois, the incumbent vendor, to continue to administer the pre-paid legal services benefit
program for eligible Cook County employees in conjunction with Pre-Paid Legal Services, Inc.
Reason:

The Request for Proposal (RFP) was posted on Cook County's website and three (3)
companies responded. Based on an extensive financial analysis and overall evaluation of
benefits from the respondents, I recommend the selection of The Advocates Group. The
Advocates Group administers benefits through Pre-Paid Legal Services, Inc. and offers the
following advantages: high level of satisfaction for Cook County employees since 2002;
responsive service and ease of administration for covered members; competitive membership
fees and a three-year rate guarantee and discount for contracted services. This program has
been in effect since May 2002 and approximately 3,500 employees are currently enrolled for
this benefit.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract period: May 21 , 2005 through May 20, 2008.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE SHERIFF
GRANT APPLICATION

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 6, 2005 from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
JACK KELLY, Chief Financial Officer
requesting authorization to apply for a grant in the amount of $50,000.00 from the State of Illinois,
Department of Homeland Security/Office of Domestic Preparedness. The purpose of this grant is to
provide funds to ensure the Cook County Sheriffs Police will be able to support the previously adopted
buffer zone protection plan. Specifically, these funds will be used to provide preventative measures
affecting terrorist surveillance and possible attacks in and around high-value/high probability targets
within unincorporated Cook County.
This grant does not require a cash match .
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $50,000.00. Funding period: July 15, 2005 through
January 14, 2008.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Chief
Financial Officer of the Sheriffs Office be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE STATE'S ATTORNEY
GRANT AWARD ADDENDUM

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 8, 2005 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney 's Office
requesting authorization to accept a no-cost grant extension from July I, 2005 through NO'>'etHber 30
October 6, 2005 from the Illinois Criminal Justice Infonnation Authority (ICJIA). This extension will
enable the office to expend the remaining grant funds that were awarded for the new Violence Against
Women Total Response Program. This program will work to strengthen the State's Attorney's response
to felony sexual assault and felony domestic violence cases with adult female victims. The Violence
Against Women Total Response Program builds upon work of two other programs in the State' s
Attorney ' s Office, the Sex Offender Prosecution Program and the Chicago Response Domestic Violence
Program. The program is designed to have prosecutors who are specially trained on violent crimes
against women (such as domestic violence and sexual assault) in both the felony review section and
felony trial sections of the State's Attorney' s Office at the Criminal Courthouse located at 2650 South
California Avenue in Chicago. The program provides specialized felony review as well as vertical
prosecution of sexual assault and domestic violence cases. The program includes four (4) assistant state's
attorney positions, specifically two (2) assistant state's attorneys in the Felony Review Unit and two (2)
assistant state's attorneys as trial specialists, one (I) in the Sex Crimes Division and one (I) in the Felony
Domestic Violence Unit.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Funding period extension: July 1, 2005 through November 30 October
Q, 2005.

1958

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Chief of the
Administrative Services Bureau of the State' s Attorney's Office be approved, as amended and that the
Proper Officials be authorized to sign on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

APPROVAL OF PAYMENT

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 14, 2005 from
JOHNNY C. BROWN, Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook County
requesting approval of payment in the amount of$67,915.17 to Total eMed/EDIX, a Spheris Company,
Franklin, Tennessee, for transcription services rendered from March 13, 2005 through June 30, 2005 on
an emergency basis.
Reason:

The new Contract No. 05-85-63 was awarded by the County Board on April 19, 2005 to
Transolutions, Inc. The hospital received communication that Transolutions, Inc. could not
implement the new contract until September 14, 2005. The terms of their contract specified
that service would start 45-60 calendar days after award of contract.
Therefore,
Transolutions, Inc. received notice that they were in material breach of the contract
This request is necessary because the failure to provide transcription services would place the
hospital in a serious situation, endangering not only the well-being of the patients, but the
ability to meet regulatory standards and generate billing documents.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $67,915.17. (897-260 Account).

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri , moved that the payment to Total eMed/EDIX
be made. The motion carried unanimously.

The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Resolution:
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

RESOLUTION AFFIRMING NATIONAL POLICY AGAINST TORTURE
WHEREAS, as elected officials of Cook County, Illinois, we have an obligation to uphold
the laws that govern Cook County, the State of Illinois, the Constitution of the United States
of America and all international treaties to which the United States is party, including the
Geneva Conventions of 1949, the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights, the
Convention Against Torture and other Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or
Punishment and related standards of international human rights; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian
contractors, constitutes a violation of the law of nations in that customary international law
prohibits torture as reflected, expressed, and defined in multilateral treaties and other
international instruments, international and domestic judicial decisions, and other authorities;
and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian
The acts of
contractors, constitutes a violation of the United States Constitution.
mistreatment aforementioned constitute a violation of the Fifth Amendment and of the Eighth
Amendment's prohibition on cruel and unusual punishment; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County, condemn the use of torture and all cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of any federal authority, including civilian contractors; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County,
call on the President and Congress to affirm the domestic and international obligations of the
United States of America to the rule of law and end the use of torture and all other cruel,
inhuman or degrading treatment as a matter of policy and to condemn the aforementioned
acts of mistreatment; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to President
George W. Bush and the Members of the Illinois Congressional delegation representing Cook
County and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.

Resolution for Communication No. 271498. The motion carried.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

SUBSTITUTE RESOLUTION
RESOLUTION AFFIRMING NATIONAL POLICY AGAINST TORTURE
WHEREAS, as elected officials of Cook County, Illinois, we have an obligation to
uphold the laws that govern Cook County, the State of Illinois, the Constitution of the
United States of America and all international treaties to which the United States is party,
including the Geneva Conventions of 1949, the International Covenant on Civil and
Political Rights, the Convention Against Torture and other Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading
Treatment or Punishment and related standards of international human rights; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including
civilian contractors, constitutes a violation of the law of nations in that customary
international law prohibits torture as reflected, expressed, and defined in multilateral
treaties and other international instruments, international and domestic judicial decisions,
and other authorities; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including
civilian contractors, constitutes a violation of the United States Constitution. The acts of
mistreatment aforementioned constitute a violation of the Fifth Amendment and of the
Eighth Amendment's prohibition on cruel and unusual punishment; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including
civilian contractors, constitutes a violation of specific protections afforded by the Third
and Fourth Geneva Conventions, including but not limited to, Article 3 common to all
four Geneva Conventions. Violations of Common Article 3 of the Geneva Conventions
are treaty violations as well as violations of customary international law; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including
civilian contractors, constitutes a violation of Articles 7 and 10 of the International
Covenant on Civil and Political Rights (ICCPR). Violations of these provisions are treaty
violations as well as violations of customary international law; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any
person under the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including
civilian contractors, constitutes a violation of the Convention Against Torture and Other
Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or Punishment (CAT), and where applicable also
of the federal anti-torture statute, 18 U.S.C. section 2340-2340A, which Congress enacted
to fulfill U.S. obligations under CAT. Violations of CAT are treaty violations as well as
violations of customary international law; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment as a
method of extracting intelligence information may lead to inaccurate and misleading
infonnation. The Anny Field Manual on Intelligence and Interrogation states: "the use
of torture and other illegal methods is a poor technique that yields unreliable results, may
damage subsequent collection efforts, and can induce the source to say what he thinks the
interrogator wants to hear"; and

1990

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon a
foreign national in U .S. custody may have the effect of radicalizing the victim' s own
The aforementioned acts of
moderate political, social or religious ideologies.
mistreatment may also have the effect of radicalizing the ideologies of the society from
where the victim originates. Radicalized ideologies may increase the threat of terrorism
against Americans; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon a
foreign national in U.S. custody may increase the likelihood that kidnapped or captured
American citizens and military personnel will be subjected to similar acts of
mistreatment. The U.S. Anny Field Manual on Intelligence and Interrogation states:
" [The use of torture and other illegal methods] may also place U.S. and allied personnel
in enemy hands at great risk of abuse by their captors"; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment
undermines the rule of law and delegitimizes the United States government as an
advocate for democracy. The U.S. Army Field Manual on Intelligence and Interrogation
states: " Revelation of use of torture by U.S. personnel will bring discredit upon the U.S.
and its armed forces while undermining domestic and international support for the war
effort;" and
WHEREAS, the U.S. Army Field Manual on Intelligence and Interrogation states that
binding international treaties and U.S. policy "expressly prohibit acts of violence or
intimidation, including physical or mental torture, threats, insults, or exposure to inhuman
treatment as a means of or aid to interrogation. Such illegal acts are not authorized and
will not be condoned by the U.S. Army." The Manual specifically defines " physical
torture" to include " infliction of pain through chemicals or bondage," "forcing an
individual to stand, sit or kneel in abnormal positions for prolonged periods of time,"
"food deprivation," and "any form of beating".
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County, condemn the use of torture and all cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon
any person under the physical control of any governmental authority, including civilian
contractors; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, call
on the President and Congress to affirm the domestic and international obligations of the
United States of America to the rule of law and to condemn the aforementioned acts of
mistreatment; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to
President George W. Bush and the members of the Illinois Congressional delegation
representing Cook County and Jet it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Commissioner Suffredin stated that this Resolution is part of a nationwide effort to protect United States
citizens, diplomats and military personnel abroad. To this end the Resolution has been modified to
include not only foreign citizens in the custody of the United States but, additionally, United States
citizens, diplomats and military personnel in the custody of foreign governments.
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Substitute
Resolution (Communication No. 271498) be approved and adopted. The motion carried.

271503

COOK COUNTY EQUAL EMPLOYMENT OPPORTUNITY PLAN (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado,
County Commissioner; co-sponsored by Larry Suffredin and Joseph Mario Moreno, County
Commissioner~.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners has instituted the
"Cook County Equal Employment Opportunity Plan" for offices under the President, and has
appointed an Equal Employment Opportunity Officer (EEOP officer) to promote equal
employment opportunity principles throughout the Cook County workforce; and
WHEREAS, in order to give such policy and procedure the full force of the County's
lawmaking powers and to ensure equal employment opportunities for persons from all
segments of the County community without regard to race, ethnicity, gender, sexual
orientation or any other protected category established by law, statute or ordinance, it is
essential to codify the affirmative action policy and procedure of the County; and
WHEREAS, according to the Equal Employment Opportunity Coordinating Council's
Policy Statement on Affinnative Action, 41 C.F.R. Â§ 60-3.17, the first step in the
establishment of an affinnative action plan is an analysis of the employer's work force to
detennine whether the percentages of persons within race, ethnic, gender or sexual
orientation groups in individual job classifications are substantially similar to the percentages
of persons within those groups who are available in the relevant job market and who possess
the basic job-related qualifications; and
WHEREAS, if substantial disparities are found, the next step in the establishment of an
affirmative action program is to examine each element of the overall selection process to
detennine which elements operate to exclude persons on the basis of race, ethnicity, gender,
or sexual orientation, and also to detennine the validity of the element in predicting job
performance; and
WHEREAS, a preliminary statistical analysis known as the "Cook County Employee
Diversity Representation Report," demonstrates a striking disparity in minority hiring among
many of Cook County's public offices; and
WHEREAS, a more comprehensive analysis of the County's work force is necessary to
substantiate these hiring disparities before codifying a Cook County affinnative action plan.

1994

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Human
Resources and the County ' s EEOP officer are directed to prepare a four year retroactive
analysis of the County' s work force to determine whether percentages ofrace, ethnic, gender,
or sexual orientation groups in individual job classifications are substantially similar to the
percentages of those groups available in the relevant job market who possess the basic jobrelated qualifications and to provide a report to the Board sixty days subsequent to the
enactment of this Resolution; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that if a substantial disparity is found through statistical
analysis, the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the County's EEOP officer are
further directed to examine each element of the overall selection process to determine which
elements operate to exclude persons on the basis of race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation
and also to determine the validity of the element in predictingjob performance; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the heads of departments and agencies under authority
of the President are directed to cooperate fully with the Chief of the Bureau of Human
Resources and the County's EEOP officer in their efforts to prepare these studies; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the separately Elected Officials of the County,
including the Assessor, the Chief Judge of the Circuit Court, the Clerk of the Circuit Court, the
Commissioners of the Board of Review, the County Clerk, the Recorder of Deeds, the Sheriff, the
State' s Attorney and the Treasurer are directed to prepare similar studies for personnel directly
employed within their offices and to provide a report to the Board sixty days subsequent to
the enactment of this Resolution.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/07/05.
Commissioner Maldonado stated the following: The Plan' s analysis would cover the past four years. At
the next Board Meeting he would supply the Committee with a list of minority groups that are protected
by the federal government. He will obtain this list from the Bureau of Human Resources. These minority
groups would be analyzed in the Plan.
Commissioner Hansen inquired how the Plan would categorize Cook County institutionally.
Commissioner Maldonado replied that the Plan would be organized by departments and agencies.
Commissioner Moreno requested that he be added as a Co-Sponsor. He voiced the concern that any
affinnative action plan advanced by the Committee must be consistent with the United States
Constitution.
Commissioner Maldonado replied that the State's Attorney' s Office has been consulted extensively
during the preliminary analysis to ensure Constitutionality.
Vice Chainnan Steele stated that a similar study was completed in 1987 which utilized yearly EEOC
reports submitted by Cook County entities.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Vice Chairman Steele, moved that the Resolution
(Communication No. 271503) be approved and adopted. The motion carried.

COOK COUNTY EQUAL EMPLOYMENT OPPORTUNITY PLAN
WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners has instituted the "Cook County
Equal Employment Opportunity Plan" for offices under the President, and has appointed an Equal
Employment Opportunity Officer (EEOP officer) to promote equal employment opportunity principles
throughout the Cook County workforce; and
WHEREAS, in order to give such policy and procedure the full force of the County's lawmaking powers
and to ensure equal employment opportunities for persons from all segments of the County community
without regard to race, ethnicity, gender, sexual orientation or any other protected category established by
law, statute or ordinance, it is essential to codify the affirmative action policy and procedure of the
County; and
WHEREAS, according to the Equal Employment Opportunity Coordinating Council's Policy Statement
on Affirmative Action, 41 C.F .R. Â§ 60-3.17, the first step in the establishment of an affinnative action
plan is an analysis of the employer's work force to detennine whether the percentages of persons within
race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation groups in individual job classifications are substantially similar
to the percentages of persons within those groups who are available in the relevant job market and who
possess the basic job-related qualifications; and
WHEREAS, if substantial disparities are found , the next step in the establishment of an affinnative
action program is to examine each element of the overall selection process to detennine which elements
operate to exclude persons on the basis of race, ethnicity, gender, or sexual orientation, and also to
detennine the validity of the element in predicting job perfonnance; and
WHEREAS, a preliminary statistical analysis known as the "Cook County Employee Diversity
Representation Report," demonstrates a striking disparity in minority hiring among many of Cook
County' s public offices; and
WHEREAS, a more comprehensive analysis of the County's work force is necessary to substantiate
these hiring disparities before codifying a Cook County affinnative action plan.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the
County' s EEOP officer are directed to prepare a four year retroactive analysis of the County's work force
to detennine whether percentages of race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation groups in individual job
classifications are substantially similar to the percentages of those groups available in the relevant job
market who possess the basic job-related qualifications and to provide a report to the Board sixty days
subsequent to the enactment of this Resolution; and
