271483

COUNTY CLERK, David Orr, by Clem Balanoff, Director of Elections, transmitting a
Communication:
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Sequoia
Voting Systems, Inc., Oakland, California, for the purchase of election equipment. The
contract is for 2,650 in-precinct optical scan ballot readers, 3,000 touch-screen direct
recording electronic (DRE) voting machines with a voter verifiable paper audit trial
(VVPAT) and two (2) high-speed ballot readers; as well as election management software,
support, supplemental equipment and maintenance provisions.
Reason:

The County Clerk issued a request for proposals (RFP), to which it received
eleven (11) responses. The County Clerk' s office selected four (4) vendors to be
finalists. The proposal of Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. had the lowest price of
any of the best and final offers that the County Clerk received from these
vendors. Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. has had great success with its DRE
system, which includes a voter verifiable paper audit trail (VVPAT). They are
the only company to have deployed a VVP AT in an election. Sequoia Voting
Systems, Inc. has a time-tested, widely-used optical scan system.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $23,754,630.00. One time purchase.
Account established contingent upon acceptance of grant.
The Chief Information Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.
*Referred to the Committee on Finance on 06/07/05.

Chainnan Daley introduced Langdon D. Neal, Chairman, Chicago Board of Elections, who delivered the
following presentation:

1997

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

The Chicago Board of Elections and the Office of the Cook County Clerk have spent two years in the
selection process of an election-equipment vendor. The following criteria were u sed in the selection
process: company reliability; ease of voter use; technological sophistication; and the ability to implement
equipment gradually to accommodate the learning curve of voters. Top-level management and staff
conducted separate reviews of the vendors; each chose the same vendor, Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc.
The election equipment chosen utilizes a dual system of "optical scan" and " direct recording electronic"
("DRE"). A solely DRE system was considered, but the majority of voting systems purchased by
governments nationwide was not consistent with the selection of a solely DRE system. However, a future
move to a DRE system is predicted.
Unlike a solely DRE system, the paper-based, optical scan/DRE system retains the following advantages
of the punch card system: security, verifiability and the ability to remake an election.
Currently the optical scan/DRE system is being tested, and negotiations with Sequoia are underway.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether the City of Chicago and Cook County would have the same
equipment and whether, as a result, the compilation and addition of data would be made easier.
Mr. Neal replied in the affirmative to both inquiries. He added that the resources of both governments
could be combined to achieve efficiencies.
Commissioner Moreno inquired whether Sequoia would have a local presence.
Mr. Neal replied: A strong presence of Sequoia in the City of Chicago and in Cook County is an
important point of negotiation. " Presence", as defined by the City of Chicago and Cook County, includes
the following: office, top management, employees and a diversity of employees reflecting the diverse
populations of the City of Chicago and Cook County.
Commissioner Moreno inquired whether Sequoia would be required to issue any perfonnance bonds
during the time of its contract.
Mr. Neal replied that this is a current negotiation point, as are indemnifications, warranties and guarantees
among the corporate entities.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether the City of Chicago and Cook County are holding separate
negotiations with Sequoia.
Mr. Neal replied in the affinnative and added that the City of Chicago, in consultation with the State's
Attorney's Office, is developing a template upon which the County can build.
Chainnan Daley introduced David Orr, Cook County Clerk, who delivered the following presentation:
The following summarizes the vendor-selection process: The process took two years. In October of
2003, prior to the issuance of the RFP, thirty equipment manufacturers from around the world participated
in a vendor fair. In March of 2004 a two-day demo session was held involving the fo ur finalists; the
Commissioners were invited to this demo session. An advocacy community was consulted periodically to
review equipment, and the Clerk's Office provided this community with updates. This community
included local civic and voting rights organizations.

1998

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

$24 million in Federal funds has been allocated to suburban Cook County by the " Help America Vote
Act" ("HA VA"). The City of Chicago has been allocated separate funds. The purpose of the HA VA
funding is to purchase equipment to replace punch-card systems and to purchase equipment that would
allow disabled voters to cast ballots privately and without assistance.
The goal of the Clerk's Office is to implement the optical scan/DRE touch-screen machines by March of
2006, in time for the primary elections. These touch-screen machines would serve the disabled as well as
anyone else who would prefer to use them. The touch-screen machines would be equipped with voter
verifiable paper audit trails as required by Illinois law. Most Midwestern states have switched to this type
of machine. The optical scan machines would be bi-lingual. The touch-screen machines, however, would
be programmed in several languages. The touch-screen machines would be utilized for " Early Voting," a
new Illinois law. A fully touch-screen machine was considered, but it was determined that the cost of
these machines would not be entirely covered by the federal funding.
The optical-scan system possesses the following advantages: It is very intuitive. It is equipped with error
detection; the system alerts a voter to his errors, which he can then fix before his ballot is cast. It registers
low rates of unrecorded residual votes. It reduces the disparities of unrecorded and residual votes among
communities at variance with each other with regard to, for example, race and income. (Detroit reduced
its falloff rate of 3.1 % (when punch cards were in use) to .7% (when the switch was made to an optical
scan system during the 2004 elections).
The Clerk's Office is recommending Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc., for the following reasons:
Sequoia was the lowest respondent of those vendors who replied to the best and final offer.
Sequoia is the only vendor, and this is extremely important, to have produced a touch-screen machine
with a voter verifiable paper audit trail. They produced, certified and implemented this machine in the
Nevada elections of 2004. Sequoia is the only vendor yet to have accomplished this. Due to the use of
Sequoia' s equipment, the Clark County, Nevada, falloff (unrecorded votes) rate for the 2004 presidential
election declined significantly.
Sequoia is the only vendor to have successfully deployed two concurrent systems: They deployed two
optical scan and DRE systems to comply with accessibility standards for disabled voters during the
December of 2004 elections in Washington, D.C.
Sequoia has been at the forefront of technology: ln 2000, the company helped Riverside, California,
become the first large-scale jurisdiction to successfully convert to an entire touch-screen-based system.
ln a comprehensive client-satisfaction survey that the Clerk's Office undertook of all vendors, Sequoia
received the highest ratings and the most glowing reviews of all finalists, particularly with regard to
service and management.
During its selection process for an election equipment vendor, Nevada' s Gaming Authority was directed
by the Nevada Secretary of State's Office to analyze the security features of both Sequoia and those of the
other finalists. The Nevada Gaming Authority concluded that the security applications of Sequoia were
superior to those of its competitors.
Sequoia has been in business for approximately 115 years. It is a United States-owned corporation based
in Oakland, California. Unlike some of its competitors, Sequoia has a longstanding policy that forbids
donations to elected officials and politicians.

1999

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

Sequoia has successfully manufactured and deployed new voting systems in large jurisdictions under
significant time pressure. For example, the company produced and deployed 5500 units in Santa Clara,
California in five months. Additionally, the company provided 7500 units for the State of Nevada in only
six months. This celerity is important given the County's time deadlines.
Commissioner Sims inquired when the machines that involve paper are expected to be phased out.
Clerk Orr replied: Federal law requires that disabled people must be provided with equipment enabling
them to vote; to this end every Cook County and Chicago precinct possesses one DRE machine. DRE
machines will be in use by the City of Chicago and the County for the foreseeable future.
Commissioner Sims inquired as to the status of curbside voting technology.
Clerk Orr replied: Only four percent of polling locations are currently non-accessible to the disabled.
The disabled population has had two exhaustive meetings with Sequoia, during which they provided
extensive input regarding the availability and development of curbside voting equipment.
Chainnan Daley requested that a letter from Commissioner Silvestri addressed to Cook County Clerk
David Orr be entered into the record and that, additionally, a letter from Daniel W. White, Executive
Director, lllinois State Board of Elections, addressed to Cook County Clerk David Orr be entered into the
record. (The referenced documents are on file in the Office of the County Clerk.)
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether it is customary for a contract to be negotiated before
certification is sought.
Clerk Orr replied that this is customary and that, further, it is essential to the current process.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether the federal funds would be paid directly to Sequoia or whether
the funds would be distributed to the County to then be paid to Sequoia.
Clerk Orr replied: The federal funds would be presented to the County, but it would be necessary to
follow a specific process. For example, regarding the punch-card buyout, upon finalization of the
contract the County would receive half of the funds, and when implementation was finished the County
would receive the other half of the funds. Both the City of Chicago and the County are in the process of
negotiating a "statement of work" with Sequoia to delineate the payment process.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether the federal funds would be available to pay Sequoia on time.
Clerk Orr replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether any other counties certified by the Illinois Board of Elections
are working with Sequoia.
Clerk Orr replied in the negative. He noted that most lllinois counties do not approach the size of Cook
County; therefore, they do not need to work with a company the size of Sequoia.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired who owns Sequoia.
Clerk Orr replied: Smartmatic International owns Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. A Dutch company owns
Smartmatic International. Some of the key investors in the Dutch company are Venezuelan.

2000

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Brandon Neese, Deputy County Clerk, provided the following additional information: Sequoia Voting
Systems, Inc., is a United States company which has been in existence under various names for many
years. During this time it has provided election services and election equipment to counties throughout
the United States. It was recently acquired by Smartmatic International. Smartmatic International is
incorporated in the United States. It is headquartered in Boca Raton, Florida. Smartmatic International
has a significant amount of Venezuelan investment. Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc., is very much an
internally managed company; its employees and management were not altered when it was acquired by
Smartmatic International.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether the product being delivered by Sequoia currently meets the
specifications put forth in the initial RFP.
Clerk Orr replied in the negative. He explained: As the project has developed and as the funding
amounts and equipment needs have changed, the RFP has evolved. All four finalists were requested to
provide additional information regarding optical scan equipment.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired why the City of Chicago and the County are negotiating separate
contracts.
Clerk Orr replied that these two governments are separate legal entities.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired whether the contracts would be identical.
Clerk Orr replied: The contracts would be similar. Sequoia has guaranteed, as a result of the dual
contracts that they would provide the City of Chicago and the County with the lowest-priced contracts
available on the market.
Commissioner Maldonado requested that Clerk Orr provide information regarding his plans for
community outreach and voter education.
Clerk Orr replied: Sequoia has significant experience in developing community outreach and voter
education plans. Negotiations are currently underway regarding the following: use of major and free
media; church-group outreach; community-group outreach; and demonstrations. Also under negotiation
is the training plan. Currently, the plan specifies that Sequoia will develop the training and educating
capabilities of the City of Chicago and Cook County staffs.
In response to Commissioner Maldonado's question regarding the budget for community outreach and
voter education, Mr. Neese replied: HA VA funding is expected to cover all capital costs and some
additional costs as well. The RFP contains a line item for $150,000 for staff training and education. The
majority of community-outreach and voter-education funding, however, will be supplied by the Clerk's
Office. There may be additional one-time costs, including: redesigning all materials; redoing the judges'
manual; and travel cost associated with perfonning additional demonstrations.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired as to the expected time interval between when Illinois certification
would be applied for and when it would be granted.
Clerk Orr replied that it is difficult to specify this time interval because the Illinois Board of Elections
would have to test the equipment, and the Clerk's Office would have no control over how Jong this would
take. He further stated that he is confident that certification would be granted within the next several
months; this would be on schedule.

2001

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Commissioner Maldonado inquired whether manufacturing would begin before certification.
Clerk Orr replied in the affirmative and added that this is the industry-wide practice.
In response to Commissioner Maldonado' s inquiry regarding MBE/WBE subcontractor participation,
Clerk Orr agreed to provide the Commissioners with specific information before the final vote.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether voting results would still be available in the polling places.
Clerk Orr replied in the affirmative.
Commissioner Hansen inquired what funds the four vendor finalists had allotted to community outreach
and voter education.
Clerk Orr replied: Sequoia allotted $150,000. The second-lowest bidder allotted $290,000. The thirdlowest bidder allotted $ 153,000 and the fourth-lowest bidder allotted zero.
Jn response to Commissioner Hansen's inquiries concerning equipment specifications, Clerk Orr provided
the following information: Most voters would stand in booths. In each booth a top screen would tilt to
accommodate varying voter heights as well as the disabled. There would be a canvas in each booth to
protect privacy. Paper ballots could be filled out in these booths or on tables that would have privacy
screens. The "Votomatic" machines would still be used.
Commissioner Hansen inquired whether there are jurisdictions scheduled to receive more HAVA funds
per capita than Cook County.
Clerk Orr replied that the majority of a jurisdiction's HA VA funding allotment is calculated according to
the size of the voting-age population. Additionally, any jurisdiction that utilized punch cards on or after
November of 2000 and is currently switching to another voting system is eligible to receive additional
funds. This funding is referred to as a " punch-card buyout." Cook County is eligible for a punch-card
buyout.
Patrick T. Driscoll, Jr., Deputy State' s Attorney, Chief, Civil Actions Bureau, State's Attorney's Office,
reassured Commissioner Hansen that foreign corporate investment in Sequoia poses no threat of
compromising the integrity of the elections system, provided that the equipment works. He further added
that the County Clerk's Office controls the integrity of the elections system in suburban Cook County and
that, additionally, this system would be purchased with Federal funds.
Vice Chainnan Steele inquired according to what timeline the Clerk's Office plans to operate to train the
12,500 election judges.
Clerk Orr replied that his Office is developing a training plan; this plan currently contains the following
components: an early launching; formal as well as infonnal training; working with political parties,
providing more advanced technical training to one judge so that he or she can train four additional judges;
and offering smaller classes. Clerk Orr further added that there will be thousands of hands-on
demonstrations.
Vice Chairman Steele suggested that the Clerk' s Office conduct demonstrations at locations that are more
accessible than polling locations, for example, schools.

2002

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

In response to Vice Chairman Steele's concern about possible pervasive equipment breakdown, Clerk Orr
replied Sequoia client satisfaction surveys revealed no such problem.
In response to Vice Chairman Steele's concern about voting accessibility for the blind, Clerk Orr replied:
With respect to equipment for the disabled, Sequoia has won several awards. Sequoia would produce a
hand-held device with earphones, through which voting ballots are read. This device would be in
compliance with the new federal Jaw that requires that blind voters be enabled to vote independently. The
blind community has provided significant input to Sequoia on this issue.
Vice Chairman Steele asked whether the new equipment would alter the time it takes to report election
results.
Clerk Orr replied in the negative, however, he offered the caveat that this is a new system.
Commissioner Moreno asked for reassurance both that the Sequoia presence would be as responsive to
the County as it would be to the City of Chicago, and that the expertise of the County Clerk's Office
would be utilized in the implementation and management processes.
Clerk Orr provided this reassurance.
Commissioner Moreno asked whether performance bonds would be issued.
Clerk Orr replied in the affirmative.
Thomas J. Glaser, Chief Financial Officer, Bureau of Finance, provided the following financial overview:
He has had no conversations with the Clerk's Office regarding cash flows related to this project. His
Bureau has neither previously nor currently budgeted funds to pay for this project. In the event that the
federal government were to fail to fully reimburse the County for the cost of this project, the County's
Capital Budget or Operating Budget would be accessed to provide funds.
There are several financing options: In the past, a special-equipment levy has been added to the election
levy and has mirrored the project' s cash flow . Proceeds from the bond issue completed in 2004 could be
reallocated to the capital project; this would require the involvement of the County's Bond Counsel.
It is not an option to advance money from the Working Cash Fund to cover this project. Because the
timing of the collection of the second installment has yet to be determined, it is his Bureau' s plan to
utilize the Working Cash Fund to cover current operations.
Commissioner Suffredin stated that, according to the State Legislature, were the cost of this project to
exceed available Federal funding, additional funds from the State would not be forthcoming.
As requested by Commissioner Suffredin, Clerk Orr confirmed the following: This contract would be
funded as a grant contract under the federal funds currently being held by the State. The contract that
would be negotiated would show the payouts as the funds were received from the State to be paid to the
vendor. At this point the County, regardless of what financial instruments have been utilized in the past,
should not contemplate using working cash funds, bond proceeds or special levies. The Clerk's Office
has no indication that the County would need funds in addition to the federal funding.
Clerk Orr stated that as a result of Sequoia' s low proposal, he expects that the County would be able to
successfully complete the project within the federal funding parameters.

2003

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Vice Chairman Steele, moved that the approval of the
contract be contingent upon receiving full funding from the State of Illinois. The motion carried.
Commissioner Maldonado requested that Tracey Graham, President, Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc.,
provide infonnation regarding the age of Sequoia's optical scan technology and how recently it has been
updated.
Ms. Graham replied: Sequoia's optical scan reader is the newest in the marketplace. It was first federally
certified in August 2003 for use in Michigan, Missouri and Nevada, it is currently being certified in
California. The 1985 model was significantly enhanced in 2003. The enhancements include: lighter
weight for easier transport; new read heads which can read a much greater variety of pencil and pen
marks and colors; and an expanded memory pack for much greater and varied retaining of ballot styles,
this is particularly important for multi-lingual ballots.
Commissioner Maldonado inquired whether Sequoia plans to wait to begin manufacturing until it is state
certified. He also inquired whether Ms. Graham has concerns regarding manufacturing deadlines
including the 2006 primary elections deadline.
Ms. Graham cited Sequoia's recent manufacturing achievements: Sequoia manufactured 12,000 units
within the contract timeframe for Florida in 2002. Sequoia manufactured 15,000 units within the contract
timeframe for California in 2003. Sequoia manufactured 7,500 units within the contract timeframe for
Nevada in 2004. Nevada's manufacturing was completed on schedule even though Sequoia was the first
vendor ever in certification for a WPAT, voter verifiable paper audit trail.
Ms. Graham detailed Sequoia's manufacturing capabilities: Sequoia has a contract-manufacturing plant
based in Oswego, New York, a contingency plant in Virginia and manufacturing capability in Taiwan.
All optical scan products are manufactured in the United States. Sequoia is considering manufacturing its
touch screen product in both Taiwan and the United States.
Ms. Graham provided the following infonnation regarding certification: Sequoia's products are already
either 2002 certified or in the process of 2002 certification: The touch screen unit, the WPAT and the
software that runs the system are 2002 certified. Sequoia's touch screen is currently in Federal testing at
WILY Laboratories, which is the Independent Testing Authority. Sequoia hopes to complete this
certification by the end of June. The Insight Optical Scan Reader is in the process of certification by
WILY Laboratories. Sequoia hopes to complete this certification in August. Sequoia should have no
difficulty manufacturing hardware product to the standard to which it has recently been tested by the
Federal Elections Authority in independent laboratories.
Sequoia will monitor manufacturing closely; it has already made significant advancements.
Commissioner Maldonado asked Ms. Graham to address the issue of the equipment's ability to count
Spanish ballots.
Ms. Graham replied: Sequoia was the first company to provide five languages on a touch screen; this
took place in November of 2003 in Santa Clara County, California. That County has a requirement that it
provide five languages on its touch screens. This was the first multi-lingual, touch-screen implementation
in a jurisdiction of that size. In terms of the issue that Commissioner Maldonado raised with Ms.
Graham, the instance referred to involved a Sequoia press team member setting up a touch screen
incorrectly. Sequoia has never utilized software uncertified at the federal and state level. It has the
capability to provide product in nine languages, including Spanish, Filipino, Vietnamese, Korean and
English. All nine languages are also available in audio ballot for use by the sight-impaired.

2004

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005
Commissioner Gonnan inquired whether any clients have voiced concern over the large size of the ballot.
Ms. Graham replied that the above-mentioned ballot is not typical in size. It is meant to demonstrate
Sequoia's capability in designing long and complex ballots. Beginning next week Sequoia will work with
the County and City of Chicago to conduct usability tests to detennine the shape of the ballot markings.
Chairman Daley asked the Secretary to the Board to call upon the registered public speakers.

STATE' S ATTORNEY, Richard A. Devine, submitting communication advising the County
to accept Proposed Settlement of $850,000.00 for the release and settlement of suit regarding
Teldata Control, Inc. v. County of Cook, USDC No. 02-C-7439. We have settled this lawsuit
in which the Plaintiff filed claims for breach of contract and quantum meruit against Cook
County. The matter has been settled for the sum of $850,000.00, which is within the
authority granted to this office by the Finance Committee's Subcommittee on Litigation at its
meeting of June 8, 2005. State' s Attorney recommends payment of $850,000.00, made
payable in two (2) separate checks as follows: the first check in the amount of $600,000.00
made payable to Teldata Control, Inc. and its attorney, Lord, Bissell and Brook, to be paid no
later than September 6, 2005; and the second check in the amount of $250,000.00 made
payable to Teldata Control, Inc. and its attorney, Lord, Bissell and Brook, to be paid no later
than February 15, 2006. Please forward the checks to Paul A. Castiglione, Assistant State's
Attorney, for transmittal.

27 1640

the sum of $25,000.00, which is within the authority granted to this office by the Finance

SECTION 11
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the recommendation
is as follows:
270979

RESTORING FUNDING OF GRADE 16 POSITIONS FOR THE MEMBERS OF THE
COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Larry Suffredin, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, FY 1997 Amendment Number 75, approved and adopted by the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County, instituted positions of support staff for the Office of the
Board of Commissioners of Cook County, and stated that " positions may be filled either on
the 110, 130 or 289 accounts with transfers between these accounts to be made at the
discretion of each Commissioner,'' and

2033

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

WHEREAS, in accordance with Section 7 of the Resolution and Annual Appropriation Bill
for the Fiscal Year 2005, approved by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County on
Februal)' 24, 2005, in which it states that "the Director of Budget & Management Services is
also authorized to transfer amounts from the 110 account to the 289 account for members of
the Cook County Board of Commissioners not to exceed the position salary available for this
purpose," and
WHEREAS, in accordance with Section 33 of the Resolution and Annual Appropriation Bill
for the Fiscal Year 2005, approved by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County on
February 24, 2005, in which it states that "the Director of the Department of Budget and
Management Services and the Comptroller are authorized to correct any factual errors in the
Annual Appropriation Bill and to implement the adopted Amendments with any required
modifications," and
WHEREAS, FY 2005 Amendment Number 33, sponsored by Commissioners Larry
Suffredin and Forrest Claypool, which "reduces funding for open positions to 9 months," and
Amendment Number 35 sponsored by Commissioners Larry Suffredin and Forrest Claypool,
which " reduces funding for open positi ons to 6 months," were both presented by the sponsors
to the Board for their approval with the intent to reduce personnel expenditures by reducing
funding for open positions; and
WHEREAS, certain members of the Board of Commissioners utilize contractual services
paid from monies transferred from their 110 Account to the 289 Account, in which case a
person is not hired and employed by the County of Cook, but is instead contracted to do a
particular task related to the member' s office, and therefore the position from which the
contractual services are paid is depleted each year and was not intended to be considered
open or vacant for the purposes of Amendment Numbers 33 and 35;
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County declares that it did not intend that Amendment Numbers 33 and 35 apply to the Grade
016 positions of those Commissioners who in prior years transferred the funds from the
Grade 016-110 Account to the 289 Account thereby depleting the funds in those Grade 0161 I0 Accounts; and further directs that the Director of Budget & Management Services remm
any monies taken pursuant to Amendment Â·N umbers 33 and 35 from tl'lese Commissioners'
Grade 016 110 Aeeounts to transfer the amount by which the Grade 016 positions at issue
were reduced from the 8 14 Account (Appropriation Adjustments) into the 110 Account
(Salaries and Wages of Regular Employees) from these Grade 16 positions.

* Referred to the Committee on Finance as amended on 05/03/05.
** Deferred at the 05/09/05 Finance Committee Meeting to 05/17/05.
*** Deferred at the 05/17/05 Finance Committee Meeting to 06/21/05.
COMMISSIONER SUFFREDIN, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER SILVESTRJ, MOVED TO
WITHDRAW COMMUNICATION NO. 270979. THE MOTION CARRJED.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON BUSINESS AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT

June 14, 2005
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County
ATTENDANCE

Present:

Chairman Collins, Vice Chairman Goslin, Commissioners Gorman, Hansen, Maldonado,
Murphy and Quigley (7)

Absent:

None (0)

Also Present:

Commissioner Claypool (I); Jacquelyn Harder - Economic Development Project
Director, Department of Planning and Development; David Dweyer - Attorney, Amari &
Locallo; and Ryan Hesch - Partner, MLRP Realty Partners

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Business and Economic Development of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County met pursuant to notice on Tuesday, June 14, 2005 at the hour of 2:00 P.M. in the Board Room,
Room 569, County Building, 11 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
271499

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Gwendolyn D. Clemons,
Director, transmitting a Communication, dated May 16, 2005:
Re:

Pulaski Partners, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 8 Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding Pulaski Partners, LLC's application for
Class 8 property tax incentive for your consideration.
Pulaski Partners, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month
abandonment rule under the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the
company can complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County.
Pulaski Partners, LLC' s application for a C lass 8, the Resolution of the Village of Midlothian
and a Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your
information.

2048

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property
Assessment Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for
a commercial facility; and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application
from Pulaski Partners, LLC and the Resolution from the Village of Midlothian for an
abandoned commercial facility located at 14441-45 South Cicero Avenue, Midlothian, Cook
County, Illinois, Property Index Number 28-10-108-035-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of
qualifying abandonment in cases where the commercial facility has been abandoned for Jess
than 24 consecutive months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was
abandoned for 12 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances are
present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners
of the County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners
indicate their approval for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate
Classification 8 abatement incentive to the company for an abandoned commercial facility
located at I 4441-45 South Cicero Avenue, Midlothian, Cook County, Illinois, under the
provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to
forward a certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
*Referred to the Business and Economic Development Committee on 06/07/05.
Commissioner Gorman stated that she is concerned with the type of businesses, auto parts and computer
retail, that Pulaski Partners is trying to put into the strip mall where there are many retailers already
established in the same type of business.
Commissioner Murphy replied that she had spoken to the Village President of Midlothian, Thomas J.
Murawski regarding the new retail shops that Pulaski Partners is bringing in, and he is in favor of the
project and feels that the new retail shops will be viable for the Village of Midlothian.
Commissioner Claypool stated that he thinks it is not Cook County's business to take tax dollars to give
an unfair competitive advantage to one business over another, which doesn' t help create new jobs it
simply shifts jobs from one subsidized retailer to one that is not subsidized over time. Further,
Commissioner Claypool stated that he questions as good public policy whether that is an appropriate
thing to do, although the Ordinance may allow technically for the application to be approved, the County
does have the discretion to object to the application.
Chairman Collins replied that she trusts that the local municipalities would be aware whether they are
putting a business out-of-business in order to create another business. Further, Chairman Collins stated
that once the application goes to the Assessor' s Office, the office looks at the application to see if the new
business stimulates the economy.

2049

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Commissioner Maldonado pointed out that there are certain areas in the County that are economically
deprived, and some of the incentive programs to attract businesses into an area is one of the few
mechanisms that the County has to be able to attract businesses to some areas. Further, Commissioner
Maldonado suggested that a study should be done to see the effect that the Classification Ordinance has
had since it was originally approved in the late 70s or early 80s, to assess the actual economic benefits
that this type of incentive program has brought into the communities.
27 1500

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Gwendolyn D. Clemons,
Director, transmitting a Communication, dated May 16, 2005:
Re:

Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc.
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation
Systems, Inc. 's application for C lass 6b property tax incenti ve for your consideration.
Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc. requests approval of the special
exception to the 24 month abandonment rule under the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution
is required so that Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc. can complete its

Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc. 's application fo r a Class 6b, the
Resolution of Elk Grove Village, Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development
staff report have been submitted for your infonnation.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property
Assessment Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level
for an industrial facility; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an
application from Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc. and the Resolution
from Elk Grove Village for an abandoned industrial facility located at 890 Lively Boulevard,
Elk Grove Village, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Number 08-27-301-023-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of
qualifying abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less
than 24 consecutive months upon purchase; and
W HEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has detennined that the building was
abandoned for 12 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances are
present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners
of the County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners
indicated their approval for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate
Classification 6b abatement incentive to Mr. Dino Krupa/Royal Transportation Systems, Inc.
for an abandoned industrial facility located at 890 Lively Boulevard, Elk Grove Village,
Cook County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to
forward a certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
*Referred to the Business and Economic Development Committee on 06/07/05.

2050

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 2 1, 2005

271501

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT, by Gwendolyn D. Clemons,
Director, transmitting a Communication, dated May 16, 2005:
Re:

MLRP 230 I Greenleaf, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 6b Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding MLRP 230 I Greenleaf, LLC's application
for a Class 6b property tax incentive for your consideration.
MLRP 2301 Greenleaf, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month
abandonment rule under the Class 6b Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that MLRP
230 1 Greenleaf, LLC can complete its application to the Assessor of Cook County.
MLRP 230 I Greenleaf, LLC's application for a Class 6b, the Resolution of Elk Grove
Village, Illinois, and a Department of Planning and Development staff report have been
submitted for your infonnation.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property
Assessment Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level
for an industrial facility; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an
application from MLRP 230 I Greenleaf, LLC and the Resolution from Elk Grove Village for
an abandoned industrial facility located at 2301 Greenleaf, Elk Grove Village, Cook County,
Illinois, Property Index Number 08-35-202-029-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 6b requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of
qualifying abandonment in cases where the industrial facility has been abandoned for less
than 24 consecutive months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was
abandoned for 14 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances are
present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners
of the County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners
indicated their approval for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate
Classification 6b abatement incentive to MLRP 230 1 Greenleaf, LLC for an abandoned
industrial facility located at 2301 Greenleaf, Elk Grove Village, Cook County, Illinois, under
the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to
forward a certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.
*Referred to the Business and Economic Development Committee on 06/07/05.
Commissioner Gorman asked how many new jobs will be created.

2051

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Ryan Hesch, Partner, MLRP Realty Partners, replied that currently the facility is vacant and falls under
the two year abandonment clause and that is why MLRP Realty Partners are before the Committee today.
Further, Mr. Hesch stated that at this time he was not able to give the Committee a direct answer, but that
type of facility lends itself to a light manufacturing assembly which typically run a couple of shifts; and
with that size of facility you can have from twenty to potentially sixty to sixty-five jobs depending upon
the number of shifts.
David Dweyer, Attorney, Amari & Locallo, stated that at this time MLRP Realty Partners intentions are
to get a light manufacturing tenant in the facility, but unfortunately without the Class 6B it is not a viable
opportunity and the deal will fall through and the building will remain vacant. Mr. Dweyer, further stated
that the only way MLRP Realty Partners can get a tenant into the building at this time would be with the
incentive, and with the size of the building and with the market as it is MLRP Realty Partners is looking
to create between thirty-five to sixty jobs once the building is fully occupied.
Mr. Dweyer stated that the building is in need of repairs and MLRP Realty Partners is looking to spend
$350,000.00 to $400,000.00 on repairing the building. In conclusion, Mr. Dweyer stated that the final use
of the building will be industrial.
Commissioner Maldonado asked who will receive the incentive.
Commissioner Murphy asked if the Committee can hear from Jacquelyn Harder, Economic Development
Project Director, Department of Planning and Development.
Jacquelyn Harder replied that the incentive will go to the owner. Ms. Harder stated that with an
abandonment provision there has to be a purchase, or in another words a new owner. She stated that
MLRP Realty Partners is purchasing the building, which at this time is abandoned and they intend to put
in a manufacturing business that will be their tenant.
Chainnan Collins asked whether the business will also qualify for tax incentives from the County.
Ms. Harder replied that the owner would pass through the property tax benefit to the tenant.
Chainnan Collins asked if this procedure was consistent with the County' s Ordinance and if it had ever
been done.
Ms. Harder replied that it has been done before, but at this time she does not have the actual numbers.
Further, Ms. Harder stated that the Ordinance requires a purchase of a building.
Commissioner Claypool asked what happens if the buyer does not get a tenant for the building.
Ms. Harder replied that the owner will not receive the incentive. The incentive is only activated with full
occupancy.

Commissioner Murphy, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved
Communication Nos. 271499, 271500 and 271501. The motion carried.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

270507

A RESOLUTION ESTABLISHING A UNIFORM METHOD FOR THE COOK COUNTY
ASSESSOR TO REVIEW THE BASIS FOR ALL TAX EXEMPTIONS GRANTED TO
REAL ESTATE PROPERTY OWNERS (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a
Proposed Resolution sponsored by Larry Suffredin, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, 88,000 parcels (excluding religious exemptions) of all Cook County real estate
tax parcels have been declared tax exempt by Illinois Law; and
WHEREAS, there is no unifonn method for reviewing the basis for such tax exemption after
it is initially granted; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Assessor annually reviews the owners' affidavit of exempt
property which states the actual use of the land; and
WHEREAS, there should be a more detailed review periodically to protect Cook County
taxpayers from tax exemptions where they are no longer warranted by the manner in which
the land is being used.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Assessor shall for all
exempt property at least every five years review the basis for all exemptions granted to real
estate property owners to detennine if the basis for the exemption is still in existence; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Assessor shall require every five years any
property owner claiming an exemption to file certified info nnation that proves the continuing
basis for an exemption exists; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that if the Assessor finds from the evidence presented by
the property owner that the basis for the exemption no longer exists, the Assessor shall return
the property to the tax rolls and the Assessor shall refer the evidence to the Illinois
Department of Revenue and the State's Attorney of Cook County for appropriate action.

* Referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee on 04/06/05.
2705 12

RESOLUTION TO DETERMINE HOW NOT-FOR-PROFIT HOSPITALS' CHARITY
CARE PRACTICES SHOULD IMPACT THEIR TAX EXEMPT STATUS (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Mike Quigley, County
Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, Cook County, following Section 15-65 of the Property Tax Code of Illinois,
exempts all property from taxes when "actually and exclusively used for charitable or
beneficent purposes, and not leased or other wise used with a view to profit" ; and
WHEREAS, not-for- profit hospitals are granted property tax exemptions as a part of this
exemption class; and

2058

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, not-for-profit hospitals have a special obligation to the public because they are
supported by the taxpayers and in exchange for their tax-exempt status, not-for-profit
hospitals are expected to serve a charitable mission and put the health needs of the
community first; and
WHEREAS, it is important that not-for-profit hospitals that receive public benefits through
tax exemptions should return that benefit to the public through their charity care programs;
and
WHEREAS, hospitals throughout Illinois will be filing reports under the Community
Benefits Act of Illinois for the first time this year; and
WHEREAS, these reports will provide information to the public about the hospitals'
organizational mission statements and will disclose the Community Benefits Plans for serving
the health care needs of the community; and
WHEREAS, other counties and government jurisdictions have already had cases that
required them to address how tax exemption status should be determined in relation to notfor-profit hospitals; and
WHEREAS, there are seventy-six hospitals in Cook County, fifty-four of which are nonprofit or church operated; and
WHEREAS, any change to the current tax exemption status would have far reaching affects
on the economic impact hospitals have in Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board, or the appointed
committee thereof, hold a hearing to determine how not-for-profit hospitals' charity care
practices should impact their tax exempt status; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Illinois Attorney General's Office, The Illinois
Department of Revenue and the Cook County Assessor' s office should be avai lable to
provide infonnation at this hearing regarding the current status of tax-exemptions for not-forprofit hospitals in Cook County and Illinois.

* Referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee on 04/05/06.
270513

RESOLUTION TO PROVIDE AN ANNUAL REPORT TO THE BOARD LISTING THE
ESTIMATED ASSESSED VALUE AND THE ESTIMATED EXEMPT DOLLAR
AMOUNT OF EACH NON-PROFIT HOSPITAL IN COOK COUNTY BEGINNING
WITH THE CURRENT YEAR'S TRI-ANNUAL REASSESSMENT (PROPOSED
RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Roberto Maldonado,
County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by Joan Patricia Murphy, County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, over seventy non-profit hospitals benefit from property tax exemptions in Cook
County and have a moral, financial and legal responsibility to provide quality health care to
the poor and uninsured; and

2059

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, in June of 2005, non-profit hospitals will begin filing an annual report known
as a " Community Benefits Plan," in accordance with state law which will include the amount
of charity care and other community benefits the hospital provides; and
WHEREAS, in addition to receiving exemptions from Cook County property taxes (which
according to independent research accounts for approximately 20% of the total annual value
of the hospital 's preferential tax status), non-profit hospitals in Cook County also may receive
exemptions from various federal and state income taxes, state and local sales and use taxes,
tax-exempt bond financing, and tax-deductible donations; and
WHEREAS, in order to qualify for property tax exempt status in Cook County, the property
utilized by the non-profit hospital must be exclusively used in a charitable manner, as
detennined by the Illinois Department of Revenue during its review of certificates of
exemption; and
WHEREAS, currently, the Assessor' s Office cannot calculate an approximate assessed value
for tax exempt non-profit hospitals and, therefore, there is no information to gauge the
monetary savings non-profit hospitals accrue through their tax exempt status; and
WHEREAS, unlike a typical homeowner who receives an exemption based on a percentage
of the home's assessed value through the Homeowner's Exemption, a non-profit hospital
receives a total exemption from the hospital's assessed value; and
WHEREAS, in order to fairly and accurately weigh the monetary value of the non-profit
hospitals' property tax exemption against the dollar amount given back to the community
through charity care and other community benefits, it is necessary to analyze the hospital's
Community Benefits Plan along with a report from the Assessor's Office that details each
hospital' s estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners
does hereby require the Cook County Assessor' s Office to provide an annual report to the
Board listing the estimated assessed value and the estimated exempt dollar amount of each
non-profit hospital in Cook County beginning with the current year's tri-ann ual reassessment.

* Referred to the Tax and Revenue Subcommittee on 04/06/05.
John M . Fallon, Special Assistant to the Assessor, Office of the Cook County Assessor, presented the
following infonnation:
Most hospitals currently receive tax-exempt status because they are considered "charitable" under the
Illinois Property Tax Code. However, Illinois law has never explicitly defined exemption qualifications;
they merely have provided outlines of a definition of "charitable." Add itionally, the Department of
Revenue has not defined how much charitable care a hospital must donate to qualify for a tax exemption.
The tax-exempt status of two Champaign County hospitals, Resurrection and Provena Covenant, are
being challenged. The Provena Covenant case is expected to be decided this summer. These cases raise
issues for over one hundred hospitals in Illinois.
The Cook County Assessor' s Office has been holdi ng discussions with groups including the following:
AFSCME, the Illinois Hospital Association, the Illinois Catholic Health Association, the Metropolitan
Chicago Healthcare Council and the Illinois Department of Revenue.

2060

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

The next presenter was David F. Buysse, Assistant Attorney General, Special Litigation Bureau, Chicago
Office of the Illinois Attorney General. He provided the following infonnation:
During the past two years the Attorney General 's Office has evaluated the effect of both hospital and
charity-care policies in relation to Illinois tax-exemption policy. The Office has conducted an
investigation of pricing, billing, collections and charity-care practices under the Consumer Fraud Act.
There was a legal challenge to the application of the Consumer Fraud Act to hospital practices. As a
result, the Attorney General 's Office has prepared "Friend of the Court" briefs in several pending civil
court cases against the Cook County hospital system. The Attorney General ' s Office has also prepared a
"Friend of the Court" brief in the Provena Covenant case. The Attorney General's brief supports the
position taken by the Department of Revenue. The Attorney General's Office has also been collaborating
with organizations throughout Illinois to create a legislative solution to problems facing Illinois hospitals
and consumers.
The Attorney General's Office has focused on the following public policy questions: How do pricing,
billing collections and charity care affect the 1.8 million uninsured people in Illinois? (1.2 million of
these uninsured people earn less than 200% of the Federal poverty level.) How do pricing, billing
collection and charity care affect the charitable tax-exempt status of not-for-profit Illinois hospitals? How
do the above-mentioned practices impact the cost of Illinois healthcare?
The Attorney General's Office has endeavored to obtain accurate data concerning the following: The
location, economic status and health-care needs of uninsured people in Illinois; IIJinois hospitals' current
policies on pricing, billing collection and charity care; and the financial health of Illinois hospitals.
(Considerable variance in financial health exists among Illinois hospitals.)
The case of Eden! Retirement Center v. the Department of Revenue is of pre-eminent importance in
shaping public policy. This verdict, a unanimous decision handed down in December of 2004 by the
Illinois Supreme Court, confirmed that the criteria for granting tax-exempt status are grounded in the
Illinois Constitution and, therefore, cannot be altered by changing the statutory requirements of the
Illinois Property Tax Code.
Commissioner Suffredin asked questions concerning how the County becomes aware of for-profit leases
on exempt land and stated that he believes county and local governments have had a significant loss of
revenue from such leases.
Commissioner Quigley stated that the County needs to do a better job defining charitable care.
Stan Jenkins, C.l.A.O., Member, Champaign County, Illinois Board of Review, made the following
presentation:
In 200 l the two major hospitals in Champaign County were tax exempt in status; today these hospitals are
on the tax roll. These hospitals are good neighbors, great employers and possess cutting edge medical
technology.
The Champaign County Board of Review analyzed hundreds of court records to determine ex1stmg
standards for the following: charity care in the community, standards for community benefits reporting,
statutes; and current case law. The handout enumerates the six criteria for granting tax-exempt status.
These criteria were confirmed by the Methodist Old People 's Home case. Additionally, the Property Tax
Code contains a basis for current tax-exempt standards.

2061

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

The Illinois Constitution, State Statutes and case law address the standard to which a charitable institution
must adhere in order to qualify for tax-exempt status. The Illinois Constitution and State statutes specify
that any institution that seeks tax-exempt status must be exclusively charitable; the institution cannot be
leased or otherwise utilized for profit. Case law further defines the term "exclusive," specifying that an
institution seeking tax-exempt status must be primarily used for a charitable purpose; this charitable
purpose cannot be secondary or incidental. The standard derived from these three sources is very difficult
for most hospitals to meet.
In order for property to be tax exempt in Illinois, the property must be " in exempt use" and " in exempt
ownership." An example of a property not being in exempt use is a physician's group leasing space from
a not-for-profit hospital. Such an institution can, however, claim partial tax-exempt status. An example
of an institution violating the tax-exempt ownership standard is when it charges an uninsured patient a
higher price for care than it charges an insured patient. Another example is when a hospital sues
hundreds of its own patients over uncollected funds instead of working with these patients to structure
reasonable payment plans. Additionally, for a hospital to be "in exempt use" it should be returning
financially to its community, in the fonn of charity care, at least as much money as it is saving in taxes.
Nor should a tax-exempt institution be allowed to use the loopholes of corporate law to achieve profit
goals, for example, transferring funds from a not-for-profit hospital into a for-profit subsidiary.
James J. Unland, President of the Chicago-based Health Capital Group and Editor of the Health Care
Finance Journal, delivered the following presentation:
In 2003, community groups began to challenge the tax-exempt status of hospitals by issuing reports
addressing the following: excessive pricing; unfair collection practices; and low charity care. The Wall
Street Journal and other press organizations ran articles concerning this topic. Recently, legislative
bodies, from city councils up through the United States Senate - have been addressing these controversies.
There are 50 million uninsured people in the United States and between 50 to 70 million underinsured
people - collectively this comprises one third of the population. At least one third of the Cook County
population is also uninsured or underinsured. These uninsured and underinsured may begin to file classaction suits against culpable hospitals.
Many people do not visit emergency rooms for fear of being overcharged and, as a result, their medical
condition deteriorates. A result of this deterioration is that the cost of their care rises significantly.
The precipitous rise in pricing and over-aggressive collection activity is a result of the financial
relationship between hospitals and insurers. An insurer is paid a percentage of the fees that a hospital
recoups. Because of this arrangement, a hospital charges higher-than-fair rates so that it can recoup more
money. Mr. Unland has interviewed almost 500 hospitals during the past two years and it is his opinion
that hospitals are not overcharging patients because of malicious intent.
Mr. Unland voiced his support for the concept of a charity-care pool; Massachusetts has implemented
such a pool, whereby hospitals with more insured patients subsidize hospitals which have both fewer
insured patients and/or greater financial exposure. In his analysis, Mr. Unland did not encounter any
hospital that recouped more than 5% of fees from its uninsured patients. In his experience, hospital
executives believe that they can collect more money from the uninsured and underinsured through fair
pricing and fair payment plans.

2062

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

Mr. Unland voiced his greatest concern regarding this issue, that hospitals are focusing primarily on their
legal rights and are suing a large percentage of their patients. As a more fair and successful alternative,
Mr. Unland cited Provena Hospital's work with a local community group. Together these two entities
were able to implement fair billing and collections practices. As a result, Provena Hospital is collecting a
significantly higher percentage of fees and sued only one patient last year. During the past two years,
various state hospital associations have focused neither on fair pricing for the uninsured and underinsured
nor on fair medical-debt-repayment plans. In this regard, it is Mr. Unland's opinion that these state
hospital associations have been severely remiss in their duties. Another consideration is that if only a
portion of hospitals practice fair pricing and billing, that portion runs the risk, unfairly, of attracting a
higher portion of the uninsured and underinsured population.

RESOLUTIONS
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 1, 2005 from
STEPHEN A. MARTIN, JR., Ph.D. , M.P.H., Chief Operating Officer, Department of Public Health
requesting approval of the following Resolution granting authority to the Chief Operating Officer of the
Cook County Department of Public Health to enter into a Memoranda of Agreement with participating
entities on behalf of the Cook County Board of Commissioners as the Board of Health of Cook County to
establish emergency public health clinics at which clinical activities, including the dispensing of
phannaceuticals, may be conducted as part of the department's public health emergency preparedness
efforts.

2063

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005

05-R-285
RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners also seives as the Board of Health of Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the Board has directed the Cook County Department of Public Health to carry out public
health activities in the areas of the County which are not served by other public health departments
certified by the Illinois Department of Public Health; and
WHEREAS, an essential function under both State law and County Ordinance is the detection,
investigation, control and prevention of infectious, communicable disease; and
WHEREAS, the department wishes to arrange with various public and other entities throughout Cook
County for possible use of sites for the conduct of emergency public health clinics ("Sites" ) which may be
activated in response to a Public Health Emergency; and
WHEREAS, an effective response to a Public Health Emergency will require the cooperative efforts of
many individuals and entities, both governmental and private, including public health departments, health
providers, police departments, fire departments and entities providing Sites for emergency public health
clinics; and
WHEREAS, as part of its response to a Public Health Emergency, the department needs to enter into
written agreements that set forth the tenns pursuant to which the department may use sites to conduct
emergency public health clinics; and
WHEREAS, these agreements will not require the County to pay for the use of the Sites for emergency
public health clinics; and
WHEREAS, it is anticipated that the owners of various Sites will be ready to enter into a Memoranda of
Agreement to pennit use of their Sites at different points in time; and
WHEREAS, in order to enable the establishment of a network of available Sites as expeditiously as
possible while maintaining the confidentiality of the Site locations until it is determined that they will be
needed in a Public Health Emergency, the department is requesting that its Chief Operating Officer be
given authority to enter into and execute these agreements on behalf of the Board.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief Operating Officer of the Cook County
Department of Public Health is granted the authority to enter into and execute on behalf of the Board,
Memoranda of Agreement with the owners of Sites for emergency public health clinics and to tenninate
such Memoranda of Agreement when appropriate; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such authority shall remain in place for five years from the date of
passage of this Resolution, unless sooner revoked by the Board.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,

ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,

ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Honoring Joseph M. Antonovich

WHEREAS, the architectural heritage of Cook County is world renowned; and
WHEREAS, preserving that heritage requires leadership, commitment and considerable effort; and
WHEREAS, in his term as Chairman of the Landmarks Preservation Council of Illinois (LPCI), Joseph
M. Antunovich has provided each of these qualities in abundance; and
WHEREAS, Joseph M. Antunovich has distinguished both himself and LPCI by decisive actions in
defense of our unique architectural legacy; and
WHEREAS, his bold leadership, commitment and effort were never more apparent than in numerous
public controversies involving our architectural heritage, some even involving matters before the Cook
County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, under his leadership, LPCI has led the nation in assisting preservation efforts through use of
private preservation easements; and
WHEREAS, also under his leadership, LPCI has provided preservation grants to some of Cook County' s
most significant landmarks, including Frank Lloyd Wright's Unity Temple in Oak Park and the Glessner
House in Chicago's Prairie A venue Historic District; and
WHEREAS, also under his leadership, LPCI helped create the most unique alliance in the history of
modernist preservation efforts, which succeeded in saving the masterpiece Farnsworth House in Kane
County of longtime Cook County resident Ludwig Mies van der Rohe.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby acknowledge, salute and honor Joseph M. Antunovich for his visionary and steadfast
chairmanship of the Landmarks Preservation Council of Illinois; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Joseph M.
Antunovich and the Landmarks Preservation Council of Illinois as a symbol of this auspicious occasion
and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.

2065

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005
Approved and adopted this 21 st day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

In Memory of Arnold "Arnie" Morton
WHEREAS, Arnold "Arnie" Morton died on May 28, 2005; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton was born in 1922 and grew up on Chicago's South Side where as a teenager
he worked at his father's restaurant; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton honorably served his country as a member of the United States Anny during
World War II; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton married his beloved wife Zorine in 1961. He cherished their life together and
his role as father to their four daughters and two sons; Arnie was also a doting grandfather to his 13
grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton gained local and national attention as a restaurateur; he opened his first
restaurant, the Walton Walk, in the 1950s; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton conceived of the idea of the Playboy Club and partnered with Hugh Hefner
and Victor Lownes to open the Club in 1960; and
WHEREAS, in the 1970s, Arnie Morton left the Playboy Club to pursue his own business ventures. He
opened several nightspots including the popular Arnie's; and

2066

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005
WHEREAS, in 1978, Arnie Morton opened his first Morton's Steakhouse in Chicago's Gold Coast
neighborhood; and
WHEREAS, Amie Morton helped create the first Taste of Chicago in 1980; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton loved his career as a restaurateur; his personality, creativity and business
savvy enabled him to create numerous successful businesses that always prioritized the customer; and
WHEREAS, Arnie Morton was respected and admired by the many colleagues and friends whose lives
he touched.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of
Arnold "Arnie" Morton and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Arnold
"Arnie" Morton so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

Honoring Harry Gadau
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau was born on June 10, 1905 in the fanning community of West Salem, he was
the first son of William and Minnie Gadau; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau moved to Chicago in 1923 after completing high school and found his first job
working for Montgomery Ward earning $18 a week; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau left Chicago for other employment opportunities in New York, Pittsburgh, and
New Salem but returned in 1926 for a job with the company that become Rival Packing Company; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau manied his beloved wife Beatrice Duncan in 1927 and their son Lloyd was
born in 1937; and
WHEREAS, Harry and Beatrice cherished their family and home life but they wanted more room than
the city offered so they moved to the northern suburb then known as Niles Center where they built a
bungalow-style home that is now occupied by their grandson's family ; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau's work ethic and keen sense for business enabled him to rise to the position of
vice-president of advertising and when Rival Packing Company was purchased in 1956 by Associated
Products, Mr. Gadau's success continued and he was made president of the dog food division; and
WHEREAS, upon his retirement in 1973, Harry and Beatrice pursued their love of travel and embarked
on dozens of trips around the world; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau was an avid gardener who spent countless hours caring for the gardens he
planted around his home which are still enjoyed today by his grandson's family; he also participated in
numerous societies dedicated to the breeding of iris and day lilies; and
WHEREAS, Harry Gadau is admired and respected by his many friends and colleagues whose lives he
has touched; and

2069

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDING S FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, Harry Gadau has lived his I 00 years to the fullest and serves as an example for all of us.
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does hereby
congratulate Harry Gadau on his I OOth birthday and wishes him continued good health and happiness;
and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Harry Gadau as a
symbol of this auspicious occasion and Jet it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 21st day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

IN MEMORY OF H. MAXWELL COKER
WHEREAS, internationally acclaimed thespian H. Maxwell Coker passed away on June 11 , 2005 at the
age of 84; and
WHEREAS, a member of the legendary Theatre Guild and celebrated Broadway performer, Maxwell
Coker received additional acclaim overseas where he starred as an original cast member of the London
production of Oklahoma and perfonned in front of the British Royal Family as part of the Royal
Command, an annual variety show in aid of charity; and

2070

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21 , 2005

WHEREAS, throughout his long and distinguished career, Maxwell Coker graced the stage alongside
numerous legendary performers including Sir Laurence Olivier, Mary Martin, Howard Keel, Vivian
Leigh, Lily Pons, Richard Burton, and Burl Ives; and

WHEREAS, upon leaving the stage after a brilliant 26 year career, Maxwell Coker shared his passion for
acting with aspiring thespians starting Brillianteen, a joint production between Evanston Township High
School and the Evanston YMCA, which is now in its 54th year of production; and

WHEREAS, in addition to teaching community youth the fine points of acting, Maxwell Coker worked
for American Express as a manager and appeared in many travel related radio and television programs;
and,

WHEREAS, while with American Express, he used his charm and wit to negotiate with the Communist
governments of the Soviet Union and China provisions that enabled American tourists to visit these
countries; and

WHEREAS, Maxwell Coker also taught in a travel industry school, lectured at the University of Illinois
on public relations and hosted a Chicago television show entitled "Its Fun to Travel"; and

WHEREAS, in 1991 , after a 30 year absence, and "just for fun", Maxwell Coker took the stage for the
final time playing the role of Sheridan Whiteside in The Man Who Came to Dinner, performed at the
Country Playhouse in Houston, Texas.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of H.
Maxwell Coker and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of H.
Maxwell Coker so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 21st day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION WELCOMING SEVENTH QUADRENNIAL
GAY GAMES SPORTS AND CULTURAL FESTIVAL TO COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, in 1982, Dr. Tom Waddell, a 1968 Olympic decathlete, founded the Gay Games Sports and
Cultural Festival to showcase Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual and Transgender sports, designing it as "an
experiment in social unity; an experiment in education; a vehicle for change"; and
WHEREAS, from July 15-22, 2006, Chicago will play host to the world and welcome thousands of
athletes, spectators and cultural participants for the seventh quadrennial Gay Games Sports and Cultural
Festival; and
WHEREAS, the Games will feature 12,000 individuals from more than 70 countries; and
WHEREAS, the competitors will participate in 30 sports, world-class athletics, art, band and choral
performances, nightly medal ceremonies, a week-long arts festival, parties and spectacular opening and
closing ceremonies featuring entertainment, pageantry, and the parade of participants; and

2073

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 21, 2005
WHEREAS, the Gay Games are open to anyone; there are no pre-qualifying events or times, just a
supportive environment, free from bigotry, where participants achieve success by their own measure.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that we, the Cook County Board of Commissioners,
gathered here this 21st day of June 2005 do hereby express our welcome to the Seventh Quadrennial Gay
Games Sports and Cultural Festival and wish them great success in their planning and preparation for the
2006 Games; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that we express our gratitude to the sponsors of the Games including
Kraft Foods and Harris Bank for making the Games possible; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be prepared and presented to the
2006 Gay Games Chicago.
Approved and adopted this 2 1st day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. T he motion carried unanimously.
